Current Affairs Commentary

The Key to Revising the Sino-US Commercial Treaty 32

Ting

According to Article 17 of the 1903 Sino-US Commercial Treaty, the treaty is valid for ten years. Thereafter, every ten years, both parties can request revisions. January 13 of this year is the expiration of the third ten-year period. The National Government proposed to the United States before then to sign a new treaty. Reports say that the US government recognizes that China has the right to request revisions, but there are two opinions on whether to sign a new treaty: agreement and rejection. This article will focus on revising the original treaty as the object of discussion.

The 1903 Sino-US Commercial Treaty has a total of seventeen articles, containing ten items. 1) Sending ambassadors and establishing official positions. 2) Residence and trade. 3) Customs duties. 4) Mining. 5) Trademarks and copyrights. 6) Inland waterway navigation. 7) Opening ports. 8) Monetary system. 9) Missionary work. 10) Extraterritoriality. Generally speaking, except for the customs duties, which were separately stipulated in a new treaty by the two countries on July 25, 1929, the most important are (A) Residence and trade, (B) Extraterritoriality, and (C) Inland waterway navigation. However, in terms of the special relationship between China and the United States, (A) and (B) are the keys to future treaty revision negotiations. We believe that the residence and trade issue should focus on the right of Chinese to enter the United States and the rights of overseas Chinese in the United States, and extraterritoriality should be based on the principle of abolishing it. Now, please extend its meaning as follows.

(A) Residence and Trade: Article 3 of the original treaty stipulates that American citizens are allowed to travel, reside, and engage in various legal industrial and commercial undertakings in the trading places of China, and are allowed to enjoy all the benefits of the most-favored-nation treatment in China. However, on the other hand, it is not stated that Chinese citizens have the same rights to immigrate to the United States and engage in business in the United States. The most-favored-nation treatment they enjoy is only limited to the taxation of Chinese goods entering the United States (see Article 5). This is a one-sided and unequal method, needless to say. Although it is said that according to the Burlingame Treaty of 1868, there is already a clear statement that the people of the two countries mutually enjoy the most-favored-nation treatment, it seems that there is no need to repeat it here. However, the Burlingame Treaty exists in name only and has long been recognized by the world, so it cannot be ignored. The US crackdown on the entry of yellow races has long been a stain on its diplomatic history. We are heartbroken and indignant, not starting today. The 1905 Chinese boycott of American goods movement was a reflection of this psychology. The Americans knew it very well in advance, so they returned a portion of the Boxer indemnity to buy our goodwill. Today, even if we do not appeal to the sympathy of the Americans on the immigration issue from the standpoint of international morality, we can also speak eloquently based on treaty rights. The aforementioned Burlingame Treaty has already clearly recognized that [changing residence and changing nationality are natural and inalienable human rights.] It also recognizes that the free migration of the people of China and the United States from one country to another is beneficial, and the two contracting parties should not prohibit it. We must know that the Burlingame Treaty is still one of the existing treaties between China and the United States. Moreover, since 1904, there has been no new treaty between China and the United States regarding Chinese immigration. Therefore, the US government, disregarding treaty obligations and international credibility, has repeatedly used its own laws to crack down on the entry of Chinese immigrants and treat overseas Chinese in the United States harshly, which is contrary to the established rules of international law. Our country's acquiescence to its actions to destroy the treaty is a matter of fact, not a matter of law. Now, in order to learn from the past and avoid future troubles, we should take advantage of this good opportunity to revise the treaty and do our best to determine the rights granted by the previous treaty. In case it is not allowed by the facts, we must also make appropriate corrections to the current methods under the principle of not harming national and ethnic dignity. As for the property rights, business rights, and marriage rights of overseas Chinese in the United States, they should also be ensured that they are in the same position as overseas Chinese from other countries, and should not be discriminated against due to differences in skin color and nationality. I think that the Burlingame Treaty already has provisions for mutual most-favored-nation treatment. In the formal negotiation meeting, the US side may not dare to overturn it. After the Manchurian Incident, the diplomatic relations between Japan and the United States suddenly became tense. Many knowledgeable people in the United States feel that it is necessary to revise the current laws on the entry of Eastern races in order to ease the anti-American sentiment in Japan. Even the leaders of California, which has always been the most fierce in rejecting Eastern races, such as the president of the San Francisco Chamber of Commerce and the president of the University of California, have publicly criticized the current system and advocated allowing a certain number of immigrants from China, Japan, and other countries to enter the country each year under fixed limits. Those who still hold opposing views are only a portion of the labor union members, which is not enough to sway the entire US public opinion. Therefore, it is beneficial to our side to conduct immigration negotiations today. Good opportunities are rare, so don't miss them. (B) Extraterritoriality: The extraterritoriality system is originally an artificial product. The various shortcomings have long been pointed out by Chinese and foreign scholars and need not be repeated. Article 15 of the 1903 Sino-US Commercial Treaty says, [The Chinese government is deeply desirous of reorganizing its own laws and regulations in order to bring them into conformity with the laws and regulations of the Western countries. The United States is willing to do its best to assist in accomplishing this. As soon as it is found that the conditions of Chinese laws and regulations and its judgment methods, and all related matters, are all properly done, the United States will immediately agree to abandon its extraterritoriality.] It can be seen that the United States also recognizes that this abnormal system is a temporary expedient. In April 1929, Wang Zhengting, the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, sent a note to the six countries of Britain, the United States, France, the Netherlands, Norway, and Brazil, requesting sympathetic consideration for the actions to abolish extraterritoriality. The US reply, although directly stated that China's judiciary has not yet been completely independent, still expressed a willingness to participate in negotiations in order to find ways to gradually abandon its consular jurisdiction (i.e., extraterritoriality), either in designated areas, or for specific types of legal rights, or both.] Later, the National Government, because there was no concrete way to negotiate with various countries, announced the abolition of extraterritoriality on its own on December 28, 1929. This move is certainly within the scope of our country's power, but the facts prove that if you want foreigners to submit to me, you must have the strength to use the last resort. Therefore, under today's environment, the only path we can take is to start with revising the treaty. Japan used this method and was able to realize its long-cherished wish to restore legal rights. Our country can imitate it. In revising treaty negotiations, there is also a distinction between joint negotiations with the opposing party or individual negotiations. In the past, when our country negotiated the issue of extraterritoriality with major related countries, it mostly adopted the strategy of joint negotiations. The result was not good. In the future, it seems that we can change our strategy and engage in individual negotiations in order to disperse the unity of various countries and leave them no room for mutual prevarication. In those years, Okuma Shigenobu's treaty revision policy started with this method and finally created Aoki Shuzo's final victory. The National Government decided to bring up the old issue again at the Sino-US commercial treaty revision conference and seek a mutually satisfactory solution to abolish extraterritoriality, which is probably with the desire to "defeat them one by one." As for the US side's prerequisite of abolishing the system in stages or progressively by event, a portion of our country's scholars have expressed sympathy. We also feel that the countermeasures to be adopted in the future should be more cautious to avoid the blame of being too eager. Treaty revision negotiations, the government should bear the responsibility of mediating, which goes without saying. However, modern diplomacy must be supported by strong public opinion to give full play to its functions. The people of our country should express their views on the upcoming Sino-US treaty revision negotiations as soon as possible to provide support for the government.

Roosevelt Announces New Currency Price

Devalues US Dollar to 59.06 Cents

Sets Gold Price at $35 per Ounce

Purchasing Gold Domestically and Abroad

White House Discusses Stabilizing Exchange Rates

(Washington) The President issued an order today devaluing the US dollar to 59.06 cents. At the same time, the President announced that the Treasury Department would purchase gold domestically and abroad starting on February 1st, setting the price at $35 per ounce of pure gold. The President also said that this pricing has no impact on the composition and value of silver dollars. The new gold dollar contains 90% pure gold, 15 and 21/5 grains equal to 59.06 cents, and is effective from the date of announcement. Regarding the issue of stabilizing international exchange rates, the President stated that detailed discussions are currently underway and that he does not want to disturb the audience, so he cannot express his opinions beforehand. After announcing this bulletin, the President immediately summoned Treasury officials and monetary experts to the White House for discussions. (31st, National Telegraph)

London Hears Like a Bolt from the Blue 33

Gold Prices Soar to New Record

(London) London received the news of President Weisford's announcement that the price of a thousand US dollars was 59.06, like a bolt from the blue, causing the price of gold to rise by 29 pence, which is a new record high. The price of gold is 135 shillings and 6 pence, plus an additional 15 and a half pence for the difference in French exchange rates.

Londoners believe that with such a high differential, profits can be made by withdrawing cash from the Bank of France. What market participants are most concerned about is what actions France will take to protect itself and avoid the withdrawal of gold, resulting in capital flowing from Paris to the United States. The export of American gold is currently purely hypothetical. President Roosevelt announced his permission to export it in order to prevent gold countries from prohibiting the export of gold to non-gold standard countries. Some quarters believe that President Luo's actions are a major blow to the UK, as he wants to force the UK to agree to stabilize the dollar-pound at a certain price. However, the British will consider this price to be an overvaluation of the pound. (1st, Reuters)

—Silver Dollar Weight Unchanged— (Washington) President Luo's announcement stated that the price of gold and the dollar are now fixed in order to stabilize domestic prices and protect commerce from the adverse effects of cheap foreign currencies. The weight of silver dollars will not be changed as a result of this announcement. President Luo has the power to change this announcement when the interests of the country require it. (31st, Reuters)

—Exchange Market Fluctuates Greatly— (London) The news that the US dollar is about to be devalued has had an impact on the foreign exchange market this morning. Various gold coins have fluctuated. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was 5 yuan and 3 points 5, then returned to 5 yuan and 2 points 75, while the closing price last night was 4 yuan and 99 cents 7 points 5. Today's exchange rate between the British pound and the French franc is 78 francs and 16/5. The development of the securities market is limited to South African gold mining stocks, and prices fluctuate frequently, but mostly tend to rise. Other securities are also active. German securities have regained their stability, as the news about debt is quite good. French securities are still strong, and British domestic industrial securities are slightly weak, but British government bonds can still maintain their prices. The price of war bonds is 101 and 8/5. (1st, Reuters)

(New York) The foreign exchange market was very chaotic after President Luo issued the announcement. All prices were opened as usual, but there were no transactions. The opening price of the pound was 4 yuan and 9 jiao 7 cents, but it later weakened to 5 yuan and 4 points, 31st Reuters

—No Different from Restoring the Gold Standard— (Washington) From an international perspective, the new US monetary policy, although not theoretically restoring the gold standard, is practically no different from restoring the gold standard. President Roosevelt's published law stipulates that the Treasury can buy or sell gold in foreign markets to maintain the price of the new dollar against gold at home and abroad. In other words, if the dollar falls sufficiently due to international trade settlement relations, making it suitable for the United States to export gold to foreign markets and unfavorable to buying it abroad, the Treasury will export a corresponding amount abroad to correct it. As for the cash export ban, it is only nominally effective in relation to private individuals and foreign countries. If the transaction between the United States and foreign countries is taken care of by the Treasury as the general clearing agency, it can freely export or import the necessary cash, that is, to maintain the price of the dollar against gold at home and abroad, so that its fluctuations do not exceed the specified range, especially depending on international trade relations. (31st, Havas)

—Impact on Japan— (Tokyo) The world's financial circles are paying close attention to the news of the US President's announcement of reducing the par value. The authorities in the Japanese financial circles have the following observations:

Minister of Finance Takahashi said that the United States has only unilaterally reduced the par value. If it does not coordinate with Britain and France, the US dollar may be difficult to stabilize. Although it has implemented a 40% reduction in the value of paper money, it may force negotiations with Britain and France. However, judging from the past relations, it may not be easy to coordinate. The stability of the world's currency cannot be easily achieved. Japan maintains a wait-and-see attitude and has made all preparations, so there is nothing to worry about. Deputy Governor of the Bank of Japan, Fukai, said that the United States' reduction of the par value is to stabilize the US dollar. However, it only does not sell gold to the central banks of foreign countries, so it is meaningless if there is no country to buy it. At this time, the two billion balance exchange funds can be activated, and the development of the situation is quite interesting. The exchange rate against the French franc may be stabilized at 6 yuan and 6 jiao 3 cents in US dollars. However, the impact on Japan and Britain, which have abandoned the gold standard, is relatively small. As for the relationship between the United States and France, it is also important because of trade relations, and only the reduction of tourists from the United States to France has a direct impact. It should not develop to the point where France stops the gold standard. However, the countermeasures of European countries in the next few days are particularly noteworthy. Okuchi Kihachi's statement said that the United States' reduction of the par value will activate the two billion exchange balance funds. There will be an exchange war between Britain and the United States. If the United States wins and the pound rises, French cash will flow into the United States, which will threaten France's gold standard. As a result, it may affect Japan, so we should wait and see how it changes in the future. (1st, Dentsu Telegraph)

Japanese Naval Authorities Express

Determination to Break the Naval Ratio

Believe This Ratio System is Not Permanent and Unchangeable

Japan's Navy Needs to be Strengthened

(Tokyo) The 1935 Naval Reduction Conference is imminent. The Japanese parliament, which is currently in session, has been discussing this issue for days and questioning the government whether Japan has prepared a strong and concrete proposal, and what it advocates is unanimously condemning the irrationality of the naval strength stipulated by the current ratio. In view of the trend of public opinion, the naval authorities have decided to resolutely oppose the revised naval treaty based on the ratio principle at the 1935 Naval Disarmament Conference. The reasons can be divided into three:

1) Taking the ratio as the yardstick for naval disarmament was invented by US Secretary of State Hughes at the Washington Conference to maintain the naval strength that is beneficial to his own country, and has no lasting appropriateness.

2) The so-called ratio refers to the ratio of quantity and the ratio of substance. Therefore, if the United States plans to build large warships allowed by the London Treaty, Japan will also have to invest tens of thousands of yuan in funding to implement the second supplementary plan, and the reduction of the national burden, which is the purpose of disarmament, will eventually become nominal, and the threat of war will be doubled. If countries such as Japan and France are forced to adopt only the lowest ratio, it is difficult to expect the safety of national defense.

3) Therefore, there is a need to implement a new yardstick for disarmament, intending to maintain the naval force that Japan will decide and advocate again at the Washington and London Conferences [sufficient for defense but not sufficient for attack] as the goal, recognize its flexibility within the scope of the minimum holding volume, and allow each country to maintain the warships that it deems most appropriate. Then the lofty goal of disarmament can be achieved. (1st, Japan United News Agency)

Avoiding Deadlock at Naval Conference 36

Preliminary US-Japan Meeting 37

Washington Considers

(New York) According to the New York Times' Washington correspondent, the U.S. State Department is considering whether to hold a U.S.-Japan meeting to avoid a deadlock at the 1935 naval conference. British Disarmament Memorandum Balances Security and Equality 38

Major Military Powers Agree to Disarm

Germany to Regain Substantial Armament

But Conditioned on Return to League of Nations

(London) The British disarmament memorandum was released tonight. The memorandum suggests that if arms adjustments and political safeguards are handled in conjunction, compromise will be easier on this broad basis.

The memorandum further suggests that continuously adjusting armaments, favoring one side over another, is difficult to implement. Therefore, it is imperative for the most heavily armed powers to abandon some of their weapons.

The suggestions in the memorandum are categorized as ensuring security, equality of rights, and disarmament. It is believed that this agreement can be achieved by meeting the major demands of all parties. The memorandum also states that Germany's return to the League of Nations is a necessary condition. (Reuters dispatch, 31st)

British Disarmament Memorandum 39

Seeking Solutions Where Possible

Europe Must Choose Between Two Paths

(London) The British memorandum on disarmament was released tonight, containing the essential statement: "[We must seek solutions where solutions are possible]." The memorandum is divided into two parts. The first part explains the reasons for issuing the current memorandum, stating that without new guiding suggestions, the reopening of the Geneva negotiations will ultimately lead to further disappointment. Discussions since March last year have proven that the British draft needs revision. The clause that prohibits certain countries from possessing certain weapons, while other countries in the world are allowed to possess them, is now clearly impossible. The British government believes that since one country is allowed to possess certain weapons, other countries cannot be indefinitely prohibited from possessing them. Europe must now choose between the following two paths: 1) Negotiate a convention in which the most heavily armed powers abandon certain types of weapons; 2) Agree on a treaty based on these powers agreeing not to increase their current armaments. The British government is eager to actively pursue the first path.

Three General Categories

Security, Equality, Disarmament

Ten-Year Term for Convention

The second part outlines the ways in which the British government believes a compromise can be reached, stating that appropriate provisions must be made under three general categories: 1) Security; 2) Equality of Rights; 3) Disarmament. Regarding security, the memorandum proposes adding three clauses to the British draft, clearly stipulating the responsibilities of signatory nations for preventing or remedying violations of the convention. This, together with the German Chancellor's proposal for a non-aggression pact, can achieve security acceptable to all nations. The British government considers the implementation of the principle of equality of rights to be no less important than the general principle of security. As for disarmament, the memorandum states that the most heavily armed powers may be unwilling to abandon their existing armaments, but the German Chancellor has voluntarily abandoned weapons of aggression. If these heavily armed powers make active contributions, they will surely enable all nations to reduce their armaments equally. The memorandum then lists disarmament suggestions, believing that a treaty with a ten-year term of validity can be established based on these.

Finding a Moderate Solution for Troop Numbers 40

Prohibit Extra-Military Training

Regarding troop numbers, the British draft previously suggested that France, Germany, Italy, and Poland should each have 200,000 troops, but Germany now demands 300,000 troops. It is not impossible to find a compromise between these two figures if other countries are willing to be consistent.

The British government is also prepared to recognize changing the military service term from eight months to twelve months. Standardizing the agreed-upon numbers should be completed within four years. Extra-military training outside of the army should be prohibited. This prohibition should be monitored by permanent and automatic monitoring agencies.

Artillery and Tanks

Germany Allowed to Possess

Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria Equal to Germany

Regarding weapons, the maximum caliber of artillery pieces for permanent borders and fortress defenses should be stipulated by international treaty. Tanks weighing over 30 tons should be destroyed by the end of the first year, those over 20 tons by the end of the third year, and those over 16 tons by the end of the fifth year. The British government agrees that Germany's new short-service army should be equipped with tanks limited to six tons. To achieve a compromise as soon as possible, the British government is prepared to agree that Germany's new short-service army can be equipped with 155-millimeter cannons. Cannons with a caliber of over 350 millimeters should be destroyed by the end of the first year, those over 220 millimeters by the end of the fourth year, and those over 155 millimeters by the end of the seventh year. The British government is prepared to allow Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria to be equipped with equivalent artillery and tanks.

Military Aircraft 41

Still Reduced According to the Draft

Germany Enjoys Gradual Equal Rights

The British government still supports the maximum limit of three tons for military aircraft as stipulated in Article 37 of the draft treaty, as well as the provisions of Articles 34 and 41, namely, that no more military aircraft shall be built except for airships, and no troop transport aircraft weighing more than three tons when unloaded. Half of the existing military aircraft weighing more than three tons should be destroyed by June 1936, and the remaining half should be destroyed at the end of the convention. Article 35 of the draft treaty stipulates that the Permanent Disarmament Commission should immediately draft the most appropriate plan for abolishing land and naval aircraft. This must rely on the strict implementation of monitoring civil aviation to avoid conversion to military use. If the Permanent Commission has not decided on a method of abolition by the end of two years, countries with military aircraft should increase or decrease them as appropriate based on the situation at the time, gradually doing so over the next eight years, so that they can eventually reach the agreed-upon numbers. Germany can therefore enjoy equal status with the major air powers through this gradual process.

Monitoring System Monitors the Implementation of the Convention 42

Naval Issues Proposed

The British government supports the chapter on naval matters in the draft treaty, but in view of the upcoming 1935 naval conference, it is prepared to adopt a simpler proposal if necessary. The British government suggests that other issues should be resolved quickly and that this agreement should be included in a worldwide convention. This move can greatly assist the naval negotiations advocated in Article 33 of the convention. If all other issues are resolved, the British government agrees to a permanent automatic monitoring system to monitor compliance with the disarmament convention. The memorandum concludes by stating that the above suggestions are intended to meet the necessary requirements of all parties and promote a general agreement, but Germany's return to the League of Nations must be a necessary condition for this agreement. (Reuters dispatch, 31st)

Italian Disarmament Memorandum 43

Strongly Supports German Demands

Mussolini's Four Proposals

Rome The Italian government today released Italy's memorandum on the disarmament conference, strongly supporting Germany's demands and stating Italy's four major demands. This memorandum announces the results of the meeting between British Foreign Secretary Simon and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in early January this year. The Italian Prime Minister's proposals include: 1) Abolishing chemical warfare; 2) Strictly prohibiting aircraft from bombing civilians; 3) Limiting the expansion of military expenditure, with exceptions for defense and engineering repair costs; 4) Limiting land warfare equipment according to the current situation. (National Telegraph, 1st)

French and German Observations Differ 44

Paris Expresses Coldness

Berlin Expresses Welcome

(London) British newspapers have praised the British government's disarmament memorandum as a brave attempt to revive the disarmament conference, while Paris has met it with coldness. Right-wing newspapers say it is difficult to accept, and more moderate circles show no excitement. Berlin newspapers have welcomed the British plan, saying it can help the discussion of disarmament. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

(Berlin) Although German newspapers say that the German government is currently conducting a meticulous study of the British disarmament memorandum, the newspapers show little satisfaction with the British memorandum and seem to have been instructed to publish a message stating that it is a pity that Britain has abandoned the position of governments secretly exchanging opinions. For example, an editorial in the Berliner Börsen-Zeitung stated that London seems to be plotting to implement its strategically predetermined goal, which is to make all talks held within the scope of Geneva. As for the essence of the memorandum, Britain intends to re-propose the conclusion of a universal disarmament convention, integrating and interconnecting the principles of equal armament rights and practical disarmament. In short, Britain's view of security and disarmament does not seem to open a new door. A local newspaper stated that the British memorandum considers not only the situation of the major countries that have been involved so far, but also proposes the suggestions of Poland, Czechoslovakia, Belgium, Austria, Bulgaria, Hungary, Japan, and other countries. Therefore, the proposal to bring the suggestions of these countries together for negotiation will only increase disputes and is of no help. The newspapers also said that the British memorandum is not a reply to the German memorandum, but at most a draft for discussion. (Havas dispatch, 1st) (Paris) Political circles are very cautious about the British disarmament memorandum and are unwilling to express their opinions, but they say that the document has been handed over to various specialized agencies for long-term review so that the government can fully understand it before expressing its attitude. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

Germany Proposes a Non-Aggression Treaty to Czechoslovakia 45

Czechoslovakia Refuses

Prague, according to some German sources, Germany has suggested to Czechoslovakia that the two countries conclude a non-aggression treaty, following the precedent of the German-Polish treaty. Some also say that this suggestion was to be made to Germany by Czechoslovakia. Officials in Prague claim that the German side did indeed unofficially probe the Czech Ministry of Foreign Affairs on this matter. The Czech government believes that there are no territorial disputes between the Czech and German states, and there is no need to conclude such a treaty, and has refused. If the treaty suggested by Germany could add some kind of guarantee beyond the Locarno Treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact, then Czechoslovakia might consider it, and negotiate directly with Berlin. Czechoslovakia would conclude friendly treaties with a number of countries, and even if it were to negotiate with Germany, it would first notify and obtain the consent of its friendly countries. This applies to the German proposition. As for the Czech side, it has never raised any matter to the German government in this matter, nor does it intend to automatically pursue any negotiations. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

No Need to Merge the Army and Navy Ministries

Japanese Officials' Malfeasance in Manchukuo

Armed Immigrants Perpetrate All Kinds of Evil

Tsumura Raises Questions

Regarding belligerent publications, how will the government crack down on them? Does the government intend to merge the Army and Navy Ministries into a single Ministry of Defense to achieve unification? Alleviating rural poverty should be approached from all sides. The cause of rural poverty lies in the poisoning of education and the excessive extravagance of weddings, funerals, and festivals. What is the government's view? MacDonald Announces Comparison of Air Forces of Various Countries in the World 47

France Has the Most Aircraft

The United States Has the Strongest Strength

Soviet Russia is Now the Second Strongest in the World

(London) Today, British Prime Minister MacDonald stated in the House of Commons that the Soviet Union's air force is now the second strongest in the world, only slightly behind France. Since the Soviet Union has vigorously built up its air force, it has now surpassed the United States and placed Britain in fifth place. Although the United States ranks third, its strength can still be called the first in the world because the United States has six times more civilian aircraft and trained pilots than any other country in the world. Currently, the world's air forces are: France first, Russia second, the United States next, Italy next, and Britain fifth. It is said that the number of Japanese air forces is also quite large. According to the latest survey of the air force strength of various countries, France has 3,000 aircraft, the United States 2,800, Russia 1,400, Italy 1,050, and Britain 850. However, in preparation for a possible conflict with Japan, Russia has now planned to be able to manufacture 35 aircraft per day. The reason for the reduction in the air force strength of the United Kingdom is due to economic reasons and the fear that Geneva will also find ways to limit the air force. (National Telegraph, 1st)

(Tokyo) Japanese Upper House member Tsumura questioned the government, saying: Japan is a founding member of the League of Nations and has contributed greatly to world peace, but when it withdrew from the League, it was recognized as an aggressor nation and denounced by various countries. This was due to diplomatic failures and excessive statements by the military. If the current situation continues, the future outcome is not optimistic. Japan must not over-rely on military force. Throughout history, many have failed because of excessive use of military force. The government should dispel foreign suspicions about the invasion of Manchuria. Various countries still recognize Japan's aggression against Manchuria. How will the government dispel suspicions? It is also heard that Japanese officials serving in [Manchukuo] are abusing Japan's power, acting perversely, and being denounced by Manchurians. As a result, Manchurians hate the Japanese very much. How will the government correct this? Regarding immigrants to Manchuria, the military calls them armed immigrants, but in fact, Japanese immigrants to Manchuria commit all kinds of evil in Manchuria, even worse than bandits. What is the government's policy? (The rest omitted)

Ascending to the Stratosphere, Russian Aviators Achieve Success and Sacrifice Themselves 50

Snowstorm Attacks the Gondola, It Does Not Fall, Three Die, Names Live Forever

(Moscow) After a night of anticipation, the Soviet Union finally learned yesterday afternoon that the personnel ascending to the stratosphere had tragically met with misfortune. Today, at the Communist Party Congress, it was formally announced that the gondola of the stratosphere balloon was discovered yesterday afternoon at the village of Boudi Juskstock, about 200 kilometers from Moscow. All three aviators were dead inside, one with a blurred face, difficult to recognize. It is said that when the balloon descended, it was suddenly attacked by a storm, and the balloon separated from the gondola and drifted away, while the gondola suddenly fell. When it landed, there were two loud explosions, and the instruments carried in the room were destroyed. Members of the Communist Party Congress praised the bravery of the three dead and decided to preserve their bodies. The most painful thing about this accident is that the three had just created a new world record for ascending to the stratosphere and sacrificed themselves after achieving success. (Reuters dispatch, 31st)

The Last Telegram from the Gondola 51

(Moscow) Today's news: a radio station near Kortigomel received the last telegram from the Soviet stratosphere balloon at 1:00 PM yesterday (January 31). Although the text was fragmented, it could still be compiled as follows: "Stratosphere balloon [electrical nitrogen] balloon has entered snowstorm boundary. Sphere faces ice. We are in a desperate situation. Two colleagues [are] in critical condition." According to the semi-official news agency, this text still needs to be verified, but the investigation committee organized by the authorities has set off to Budeski village today to inspect the destroyed balloon and the corpses of the deceased. It has been decided to bury the remains of the three victims alongside the wall of the government office, so that the names of the heroes will live forever. (National Telegraph, 1st)

Sun-Ma Conflict: Fierce Fighting in Ningsuo Huangxia Fengdeng 90

Ningxia requests all stationed troops to encircle and attack Sun's army. Sun Dianying commands troops westward at Baofeng headquarters. He Yingqin plans to send someone to meet with Sun to discuss a ceasefire. Sun's troop strength expanded to more than 20 regiments.

(Beiping Correspondence): The conflict between Sun and Ma's troops was most intense around the 26th and 27th. Sun Dianying aimed to occupy the provincial capital of Ningxia, advancing in three routes. The main force, led by Yang Huifeng's 110th Division (i.e., Yang Houxiao's troops) and Wang Ying's troops from Ligangpu, advanced towards Ningxia. The left flank, led by Yu Shiming, commander of the cavalry army, supervised Zhao Guozhen's 2nd Cavalry Division and Shi Wenhua's 3rd Cavalry Division, advancing along the east bank of the Yellow River towards Ningxia. The right flank, consisting of Ding Futing's 117th Division, Liu Yueting's 118th Division, and Liu Guangde's artillery regiment, secretly crossed the Helan Mountains from Niubagou under the command of Liu Yueting. They arrived at Huangxia Pass near Ningcheng on the evening of the 26th. At 3 a.m. on the 27th, they sent more than 3,000 plainclothes soldiers, each carrying a pistol, from Huangxia Pass to outside the Ningxia county seat, scaling the city walls with cloud ladders to attack the provincial capital of Ningxia. The defending garrison consisted of Ma Hongkui's guard brigade, a regiment from Hu Zongnan's troops, and a brigade from Ma Bufang's troops. They immediately used machine guns to sweep the area, resulting in approximately 1,000 casualties among Sun's troops who fell from the city walls. Ma's troops suffered more than 100 casualties. At dawn, the fighting subsided slightly. In the afternoon, the 35th Division of Ma Hongbin's troops outflanked Liu Yueting's troops, who retreated after suffering losses. The Ningxia security police and the Han and Lu brigades, together with Ma Hongbin's troops, advanced to block them, and Sun's troops retreated to the Fengdengpu and Mandaqiao areas northwest of Ningcheng. Sun Dianying rushed to transfer Lu Fengnian's 119th Division stationed in Baotou to reinforce them. On the 29th, fierce fighting broke out again between the two armies outside the Ningxia county seat. Sun's army adopted a guerrilla-style sudden attack tactic. The Ningxia army attacked Huangxia Pass, Fengdengpu, and Mandaqiao on the 30th, and the fighting was still extremely fierce. However, since Sun's army continued to receive reinforcements from Baotou, Linhe, and Wuyuan, it would be difficult to retreat unless pressure was applied to its rear. It is reported that the Ningxia side has requested a certain military authority to quickly order Yan Xishan to instruct Fu Zuoyi, Wang Jingguo, and other troops to block Sun's army's rear, and to request that Xu Tingyao's 17th Army stationed in Baoding be sent to Baotou to encircle and attack. According to an aide-de-camp of Sun's army who came to Beiping from the front lines, the majority of Sun's troops are concentrated in the Pingluo Ligangpu area, and another force is advancing towards Ningxia, with the front lines already reaching the Beita area in the suburbs of Ningxia, and the military situation is quite favorable. This proves that the news of Sun's army retreating east of the Yellow River is likely a false report. Sun Dianying's director of the office in Beiping, Wang Shiping, visited He Yingqin on the afternoon of the 30th, requesting that someone be sent to Dengkou to investigate the truth. He then stated that in the event of a conflict between Sun and Ma's armies, it is imperative to seek a solution. The first step is for both sides to cease fire. Only after receiving telegrams of a ceasefire from both sides in Beiping can the Military Council send someone to Dengkou to discuss follow-up measures with Sun Dianying. If both sides still do not cease fire, then there is no need to send anyone. Wang replied that there is absolutely no problem with Sun's troops ceasing fire, but to prevent pursuit, it is difficult to withdraw troops before a solution is found, so he urgently hopes that the authorities will dispatch high officials to go immediately. He is currently selecting someone for the dispatch of high officials, and it is rumored that the Military Council will send member Ji Yiqiao to inquire. When they will depart is currently undecided. As for He Yingqin's representative, Men Bingyue, who was sent to the Northwest some time ago, is currently still in Suiyuan and has not gone to Baotou. He must wait until the Sun Dianying and Ma Hongkui conflict is resolved before returning to Beiping. Sun Dianying himself is currently commanding military operations in Shifeng. Sun's rear is extremely busy with troop movements, indicating that the war is still ongoing.

According to a telegram from Ningxia received by the 15th Route Army's office in Beiping, since Sun Dianying's troops occupied Dengkou County on the morning of the 12th, they have been advancing westward, already pressing on Ningxia. The chairman of Ningxia Province, Ma Hongkui, initially did not dare to lightly start a war because he had not received a central order to resist, so he urgently telegraphed the Central Government and Zhu Shaoliang, the Pacification Commissioner of Gansu, to report the details and request instructions. Chiang Kai-shek and Zhu Shaoliang both sent replies to Ningxia, strictly ordering them to block the attack. Chiang's telegram stated, "[Sun's troops were previously ordered to temporarily stay in their original defenses and await orders. If they rashly advance, they are acting recklessly. I hope you will follow Commissioner Zhu's orders and do your best to prevent and block them, without any hesitation.]" Zhu's telegram stated, "[Sun's troops are disobeying orders and advancing westward, invading Dengkou, colluding with bandits and communists, and disrupting the local area. You should take appropriate self-defense and severely attack them. The group telegram has been noted.]"

Sun Dianying's troops originally belonged to Zhang Zongchang's command. In the autumn of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], Sun's troops moved to southern Shanxi. Later, the Northeastern Army entered the customs, and Sun repeatedly sent people to negotiate incorporation. At that time, Zhang Xueliang was ordered to reorganize the military and political affairs of North China, and he convened a meeting of generals in Tianjin. At that time, it was agreed that Sun's troops would be reorganized into the Provisional 2nd Army Division, commanding two infantry brigades, a total of four regiments. In the spring of the 20th year of the Republic [1931], the Central Government revised Sun's troops to be the 40th Army Division, with the two brigades under its command being the 117th Brigade and the 118th Brigade, each with two regiments. Sun's troops also requested additional编制due to the excessive number of personnel, and Zhang Xueliang approved the addition of three infantry regiments, totaling seven infantry regiments before and after, as well as the division headquarters' directly-subordinated guard battalion, heavy mortar battalion, etc. At this time, according to its编制, the monthly经费paid was more than 190,000 yuan. In the autumn of the 20th year of the Republic, during the campaign against Shi Yousan, Sun's troops were ordered to be reorganized into the 41st Army, commanding the original troops of the division, and they were allowed to increase the monthly经费by 30,000 yuan, totaling more than 220,000 yuan. At this time, in addition to the prescribed seven regiments, Sun's troops secretly expanded several units. In the spring of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], the anti-Japanese war broke out, and Sun's troops were ordered to participate in the war. Before being ordered to depart, they requested an increase in经费. The Military Council approved an increase of 80% of the給養for 8,000 people, approximately 20,000 yuan. At the end of the war, all the vehicles in North China were ordered to be缩编, and Sun's troops still maintained the original plan of seven infantry regiments, as well as various directly-subordinated special battalions and companies, etc. The经费was still 220,000 yuan according to the original plan, and only about 1,000 yuan was deducted from the unit's经费according to the比例of 缩编of each army. However, although the unit was still nominally seven regiments at this time, it actually secretly 收编scattered soldiers and bandits in the Chahar territory, more than doubling the number of personnel approved by the Military Council. Later, when the unit moved to western Suiyuan, it again 收编local bandits such as Yang Houxiao and Wang Ying, and privately expanded the troop numbers greatly, totaling four infantry divisions, namely the 117th, 118th, and 119th divisions, each with three brigades, each with three regiments, the 120th division with two brigades and one special service regiment, and one replenishment brigade, three cavalry divisions, each with three regiments, and three cavalry brigades, each with two regiments, one artillery brigade, three engineer and transport battalions, and two gendarmerie battalions, totaling more than 30 regiments. Those approved by the Military Council should be seven infantry regiments, and the monthly经费was more than 220,000 yuan. Since the unit privately expanded more than 20 regiments, it was only natural that its 支給was insufficient. This is why the army was so eager to move westward in order to gain a territory.

Central Army Advances to Suppress Red Bandits in Northern Fujian 91

Large numbers of Red bandits discovered in Shouning, with Chen's regiments having already split up to intercept them.

(Fuzhou Communication): The remnants of the 19th Route Army, who had fled to Quanzhou and Yongchun in southern Fujian, were surrounded on all sides because Zhangzhou and Xinghua had been recaptured by the Central Army. They telegraphed to declare their allegiance and were granted amnesty. Chiang Kai-shek replied with an order, limiting them to three days to depart from Quanzhou and Yongchun and concentrate in the three counties of Hui'an, Putian, and Fuqing to await reorganization. The deadline has now passed, but the army has not yet complied with the order to depart. Therefore, the Central Army is still departing from Xiamen to Tong'an and Xinghua to Hui'an, strictly preventing them from fleeing again. As for the Red bandits who harassed Yong'an, Sha County, Youxi, Jiangle, Shunchang, and Yangkou in northern Fujian, Wei Lihuang, the commander-in-chief of the 5th Route Army, has transferred Leng Xin's 3rd Division to attack the bandits in Sha County. They have been engaged in fierce fighting with the bandits in the Qingzhou and Caodi areas of Sha County for days. Lu Xingbang's 55th Division has also been transferred from Datian to Youxi. According to yesterday's news, the forward troops have approached the county seat and can coordinate with Leng's Division to closely surround the bandits in Sha and You counties. The air force will then conduct bombings. In Shunchang, Zhao Guantao's army stationed on the Fujian-Zhejiang border is leading a force of two divisions from Pucheng and Chong'an to Jian'ou and Jianyang, advancing towards Yanping and Shunchang. Chen Cheng's army stationed on the Fujian-Jiangxi border is leading three divisions from Zixi and Lichuan to Guangze and Shaowu, advancing towards Jiangle and Taining, coordinating with Liu Heding's and Zhou Zhiqun's divisions to first consolidate the border defenses and then blockade the bandit areas to cause their collapse. Furthermore, in Shouning in eastern Fujian, more than 3,000 Red bandits have recently been discovered, attacking the Nanyang Township in the western district of the county, looting and burning extensively, and spreading to Saiqi Town in Fu'an County. Chen Qixuan's newly formed 10th Division has ordered Liu Jun, Chen Zheng, and Gu Hongyang's regiments to split up and intercept them. It has been determined that the Red bandits' invasion of eastern and northern Fujian was instigated by the 19th Route Army, causing harm to the local areas. (January 27th)

New Fujian Provincial Committee Chairman Chen Yi Arrives in Fujian 92

│New provincial government opening expenses are being discussed with the Chamber of Commerce│

Fuzhou Communication: The members of the Fujian Provincial Government have been announced for many days. Chairman Chen Yi, because he was in Beijing to negotiate important matters with Lin, Wang, and Chiang, delayed his departure from Beijing to Shanghai until January 25th. On the 29th, accompanied by Zheng Zhenwen, Director of the Education Department, Chen Ticheng, Director of the Construction Department, and Wei Datong, President of the High Court, he came to Fujian from Shanghai aboard the Ninghai naval warship. At 4 p.m. on the 30th, he arrived safely in Magong. Officials from the provincial government and the civil affairs, education, and construction departments all went to Magong to welcome him. The entire city also hung national flags to express welcome. When the Ninghai warship entered the port, warships anchored on the river surface fired salutes to pay their respects. The various steamships that welcomed him also set off firecrackers, making it very lively. Chen Yi and others came out of the cabin to nod their greetings to those who welcomed him, and then changed to the Haiping steamship, arriving at Taijiang at 6 p.m., disembarking in front of the Naval Public Office in Zhongzhou, changing to cars and entering the city to go to the provincial government. At this time, the inside and outside of the provincial government had been newly decorated, and the electric lights were brightly lit. After entering the government and meeting with various important party, government, and military figures, Chen went to the Sa Family Garden in Tangjing Alley at 7 p.m. to attend a banquet hosted by Commander Chen Jiliang, which did not end until after 9 p.m. He stayed at the Third Bridge Club outside the Water Gate. On the morning of the 31st, he paid a visit to Commander-in-Chief Chiang Dingwen and Commander Chen Jiliang to discuss matters concerning Fujian. In the afternoon, representatives from all walks of life visited the provincial government in an endless stream, and Chen himself and Secretary-General Gao Dengting received them separately. According to Chen, after the establishment of the new provincial government, the first priority is to restore the original state of the region. To restore the original state, we must start by reorganizing the remnants of the民军and整理财政. After taking office, he will immediately discuss implementation methods with all relevant parties. As for the provincial government and the various departments, it is scheduled to be taken over on February 1st, and the swearing-in ceremony will be held on the 3rd. The members currently in the province are Chen Yi, Xu Fu, Zheng Zhenwen, and Chen Ticheng. Li Shijia and Lin Zhiyuan will also fly from Xiamen to the province on the 2nd to participate. Sun Jiazhe, Sun Xiwu, and Li Qingquan are in Guangdong, Shanghai, and Nanyang, respectively, and it has not yet been decided whether they will come to Fujian. The position of Director of the Finance Department will probably be filled by Xu Fu on an acting basis. Fujian Province is in a difficult financial situation due to the initial pacification after the great turmoil, and the military affairs have not been completely concluded. Therefore, all agencies have adopted a austerity policy. The old staff of the provincial government and the four departments will be audited to determine who to keep and who to dismiss. It is rumored that more than one-third of the redundant employees will be laid off. As for financial issues, Xu Fu is currently making detailed plans to comprehensively manage all national and local taxes and levies in the name of the special financial agent of the Xingying. Before the establishment of the new provincial government, all revenue will be temporarily handed over to the Fuzhou Xingying for military use. Regarding the opening expenses of the new provincial government, negotiations are underway with the Chamber of Commerce to borrow 300,000 yuan for use. The Chamber of Commerce was affected by the disturbance of the Red bandits in northern Fujian in the autumn of last year, and the变乱of the 19th Route Army in the winter. The market is extremely depressed. It is now housing refugees from northern Fujian in the southern countryside and逆军from Nantai, totaling about 4,000 people. The给养is very expensive, and the planning is extremely difficult. It is currently discussing relief measures with the authorities. (January 31st)

Xie Rongqing, the chief accountant of the County Stamp Tax Bureau, and Yang Yongqing, the inspector, went to Qishi Town to inspect stamp duty. When they inspected the Dafeng Clothing Store, for some unknown reason, they overturned the account books and goods indiscriminately. The store believed that this was unreasonable and called the police to the scene to testify. Xie and others realized that they were in the wrong. After mediation by the town police station and the district office, Xie wrote a letter of apology to settle the matter. However, after Xie returned to Songjiang, he claimed that the clothing store's account books had underpaid stamp duty and published it in the county newspaper. The business community in the town was in an uproar. The patrol officer of the town police station then wrote a letter to prove that the store had not underpaid stamp duty, as well as the situation of Xie and others' inspection causing trouble and apologizing on that day. However, Xie still did not repent, claiming that the patrol officer had been dismissed and that his testimony was insufficient. Therefore, the new patrol officer, based on the original files taken over, issued another statement, and Xie and others' illegal actions were met with increasing uproar. It is now known that the town's士商have jointly presented a public petition to the Provincial Stamp Tax Bureau and the county government, requesting a thorough investigation and punishment to appease public anger.

The Jiangsu Private Smuggling Headquarters divides Jiangsu Province into eight regions. The chiefs below the regional chief are the sub-regional chiefs, and the team captains are stationed in various places to investigate and combat smuggling. The sub-regional department stationed in Caohujing County closed down yesterday (31st).

Robbers Devise a Plan to Steal Wealth 98

Zhang Sheng, a resident of Jishui Port in Zhongdai Town, which is under the jurisdiction of the county, makes a living by fishing. His family is quite well-off. Pinghu

Misunderstanding and Disturbance in Maogou Town 99

The Public Security Bureau of this county received a tip-off that a large batch of smuggled soil had been brought in by night ferry. They dispatched eight officers to intercept it at Maogou. The officers hired a small boat to go there, and fearing a leak of information, they all wore plain clothes. As soon as they landed, they heard the sound of gongs ringing from afar. A large group of militia rushed over, and the gunfire was very dense. The officers did not know what to do. Fortunately, the boatman was quick-witted and shouted that they were police officers from Pinghu on official business, and the shooting finally stopped. Most of the residents were already terrified and scattered in all directions. Then, the militia came up to search, stating that the recent frequent occurrence of burglaries had caused a misunderstanding in the local villagers' report. They apologized and left. The officers also returned, thoroughly shaken.

Soong Tzu-wen Discusses the Future Work of the Economic Council 102

Three Standing Committee Meetings Discussed Seven Proposals

Cotton and Wheat Loan Under Negotiation for Amendment

A Plenary Meeting Has Not Been Scheduled Yet

Soong Tzu-wen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council, received reporters from various newspapers at his private residence on Qiqi Road at 11:00 yesterday morning to report on the recent work of the Economic Council, saying that a plenary meeting of the Committee would be convened after the general policy directions were determined to decide on specific measures. Mr. Soong's remarks are recorded as follows:

Standing Committee Discusses Proposals from Various Parties 103

Mr. Soong first stated that the Standing Committee meeting had discussed proposals from various parties, including (1) Highway Planning, (2) Shipping Planning, (3) Public Water Conservancy, (4) Cotton and Silk Industry, (5) Northwest Development, (6) Jiangxi Development, and (7) Agricultural Hygiene. After discussion, it was agreed that two or three of these items should be selected for implementation first to concentrate efforts and achieve significant results more easily. If all items were to be implemented simultaneously, it was feared that there would not be enough resources, which would be inappropriate. As to which items should be selected first, it still requires careful study by the Standing Committee.

Plenary Meeting Not Yet Scheduled 104

Mr. Soong also stated that the date for convening a plenary meeting of the Economic Council has not yet been set. The Standing Committee must carefully study the above-mentioned proposals from various parties and select the projects that should be implemented in advance. Only after determining that it is necessary to convene a plenary meeting for discussion will the date of convening be decided.

Cotton and Wheat Loan Under Negotiation for Amendment 105

When reporters inquired about amending the US cotton and wheat loan agreement, Mr. Soong stated that because domestic cotton and wheat production had been very strong last year, coupled with the low price of cotton yarn, the imported US cotton and wheat were not selling well. Therefore, it was necessary to negotiate an amendment with the US to reduce the amount purchased or transfer the funds to purchase other goods. This is currently being handled by the embassy secretary, Mr. Wei Wenbin, in the US. As for the funds obtained from the sale of US cotton and wheat that have already arrived in Shanghai, they are still deposited in the bank and have not been touched.

Soong Denies Restructuring of the Economic Council 106

There were rumors that the Economic Council would be changed to a chairman system. When reporters asked Mr. Soong about this, he said that there was no such thing as changing the Economic Council to a chairman system, but it was planned to set up a director of operations, to be concurrently held by a member of the Standing Committee. During discussions in Nanjing, several members of the Standing Committee proposed that he concurrently serve as the director of operations, but he felt that the responsibility was heavy and the work was complicated, and he was afraid that he would not be able to handle it, so he did not take the position.

Implementation of the Seven-Province Highway Plan 107

Mr. Soong continued, "In the past, the Council's funds have mostly been used for highway construction. The Council itself does not use much money. However, the two-year highway construction plan for seven provinces will begin this year, which is the first year. As for the Council's relationship with the various provinces, it is only in the position of providing subsidies and supervision. That is, it allocates funds to subsidize those provinces that meet the Council's highway construction plan standards to promote its implementation and supervises it at any time during the process." Mr. Soong also stated that whether or not to organize the Coal and Cement Control Committee is still under study by the Standing Committee.

Soong Has a Very Good Impression of the Plenary Meeting 108

Mr. Soong concluded by saying that everyone was able to unite in spirit during this plenary meeting, and he had a very good impression of it. He did not make any proposals himself, but only gave a brief and systematic oral report on the past affairs of the National Economic Council and the negotiations he had conducted overseas.

Guo Shun Was Publicly Elected as Chairman

Consulted with the Ministry of Industry on Economic Issues

The preparatory committee for the National Production Conference held its first preparatory committee meeting at the China Industrial Federation at No. 9 Hankou Road at 3:00 p.m. yesterday.

Attending Committee Members Besides Liu Yinfei, Director of the Industrial Department of the Ministry of Industry, the attendees yesterday included preparatory committee members Guo Shun (representing Zheng Yizhi), Qian Chengxu, Mu Ouchu, Wu Yunzhu, Wang Yunwu (representing Qian), Cai Shengbai, and Hu Xiyuan, totaling seven people. General Situation of Revenue and Expenditure of the Two Railways Last Year 110

Estimated Total Revenue for the Whole Year

Statistics on Repaying Outstanding Debts

The amount of revenue and expenditure of the two railways in 1933 is investigated as follows: The total operating revenue of the two railways throughout the year, plus income from rent and interest, is approximately 14.18 million yuan for the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and approximately 6.8 million yuan for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, totaling 20.98 million yuan. The operating expenses, plus debt interest, government capital interest, and other miscellaneous expenses, are approximately 12.5 million yuan for the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and approximately 5.47 million yuan for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, totaling 17.97 million yuan. The difference between revenue and expenditure is approximately 3.01 million yuan in surplus. As for the various outstanding debts repaid successively this season, in addition to the outstanding materials debts of 134,826.16 yuan from before 1932, all are overdue debts owed to the Chinese-British Bank Corporation. For the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, they include: (1) the second installment of the principal for the advance payment for the purchase of vehicles, 138,240 yuan; (2) the interest on the loan due on May 18, 1932, plus bank commissions, 1,076,032.77 yuan. For the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, they include: (1) the principal of the 29th and 30th installments, plus a portion of the bank commissions, 939,900.13 yuan (including 440,000 yuan allocated by the Ministry of Railways); (2) the remaining amount of the principal plus bank commissions of the previous item, and overdue interest, 232,500 yuan (funds allocated by the Ministry of Railways); (3) the interest on the 31st installment plus bank commissions, 173,927.71 yuan. In total, the two railways paid a total of 2,560,600.61 yuan. Including the public funds for materials repaid this season, the total is 2,695,426.77 yuan. If we include the previous three seasons, the total principal and interest of various loans and advances repaid to the Chinese-British Bank Corporation in 1933 is 4,635,481.37 yuan. If we further add the unpaid amounts from before 1932, (1) outstanding joint transportation debts of various railways, 476,421.14 yuan; (2) outstanding materials debts from various parties, 856,366.83 yuan, then the total amount of outstanding debts repaid throughout the year is 5,968,269.34 yuan (including 672,500 yuan allocated by the Ministry of Railways).

The Sino-British Telecommunications Link Will Open Tomorrow 111

Minister Zhu Will Come to Shanghai Tonight to Participate

Minister Zhu's Wife Will Perform the Inauguration Ceremony

According to the Central News Agency, the Sino-British Direct Telecommunications Link, organized by the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, has been fully completed and is scheduled to hold the opening ceremony of the Sino-British Direct Telecommunications Link at the Zhenru International Radio Station at 3:00 p.m. tomorrow. The Minister of Communications, Zhu Jia-hua, is scheduled to come to Shanghai from Nanjing tonight to participate in the ceremony. The inauguration ceremony will be performed by Minister Zhu's wife, Madam Cheng Pei-fang. The details of the preparations and other information are recorded as follows:

Minister Zhu Will Come to Shanghai Tonight to Participate 112

The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held at the Zhenru International Radio Station at 3:00 p.m. tomorrow. All arrangements have been made. Minister Zhu Jia-hua telegraphed the International Telecommunications Bureau yesterday, saying that he had decided to come to Shanghai to participate in the ceremony. It is also learned that Mr. Zhu has decided to take the night express train from Nanjing to Shanghai tonight with his wife, Madam Cheng Pei-fang. Madam Zhu has also agreed to perform the inauguration ceremony. After the opening ceremony, there will be a tea party at Zhu's residence on Seymour Road at 6:00 p.m.

Two Years of Preparation Fully Completed 113

In view of the increasingly close relationship between China and Britain, and the fact that telecommunications between the two countries relied entirely on foreign merchants, which not only meant the loss of sovereignty but also caused inconvenience, the Ministry of Communications first signed the Sino-British Wireless Telegraphy Agreement with the Imperial International Communications Company in London in June 1932 and signed a contract with the Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company in London to purchase Marconi high-power wireless telegraph and telephone transmitting and receiving equipment. In July, the International Telecommunications Bureau was instructed to allocate 100,000 yuan from the deposit of telegraph fees as a guarantee deposit for the contract to purchase equipment from the Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company. It then prepared for the implementation of various tasks related to the Sino-British Telecommunications Link and dispatched four trainees to the Marconi Company for practical training in March of last year. The construction of the radio station building began in April, and the first batch of ordered equipment arrived in Shanghai at this time. In May, the construction of the antenna tower and other projects began. As for the foundation stone laying ceremony for the British machines, it was held in June by Minister Zhu himself in Shanghai. The laying of underground cables, the erection of antennas, and the installation of the delivered equipment were all completed at the beginning of last month and trial reports were started. Marconi Company sent engineer Henry to Shanghai to assist with everything.

Total Expenditure of 1.2 Million 114

The equipment for the Sino-British Telecommunications Link is a Marconi high-power direct-wave radio telegraph machine. The total price of the transmitting and receiving telephone machines is 742,344.083 yuan, freight and insurance are 18,400 yuan, customs duties are 159,641.621 yuan, the generator is 71,000 yuan, the central transmitting and receiving room equipment is 26,251.023 yuan, the base totals 17,989.043 yuan, the buildings total 48,889.084 yuan, the equipment installation fee totals 64,734.08 yuan, and the underground cables total 105,087.082 yuan, totaling 1,254,349.58 yuan.

Both Parties Decide on Telegraph Fee Distribution 115

The Sino-British Telecommunications Link is scheduled to open tomorrow and begin telecommunications immediately, as the results of the trial reports in recent days have been exceptionally good. As for the telegraph fees collected, they are equal to the prices of foreign merchants. The method of distribution of the telegraph fees collected between China and Britain has also been decided. Two-thirds of the telegraph fees from China to Britain will belong to us, and the rest will belong to Britain. From Britain to China, the opposite is true. For example, if a telegram is sent from Shanghai to London and the price is 100 yuan, then 75 yuan will belong to our side and 25 yuan will belong to the British side.

Telecommunications in Various Places Gradually Expanding 116

The Bureau is gradually expanding direct telecommunications with foreign countries. Including the Sino-British link, it has reached eleven locations, including (1) Shanghai-Manila, telecommunications began on January 4, 1929, (2) Shanghai-Hong Kong, telecommunications began on July 1 of the same year, (3) Shanghai-Batavia, telecommunications began on May 7, 1930, (4) Shanghai-San Francisco (jointly operated company radio station), (5) Shanghai-Berlin, (6) Shanghai-Paris, all of which began telecommunications on December 6, 1930, (7) Shanghai-Saigon, telecommunications began on July 1, 1931, (8) Shanghai-Geneva, telecommunications began on February 5, 1932, (9) Shanghai-Moscow, telecommunications began on March 10, 1933, (10) Shanghai-San Francisco (Mackay Company radio station), telecommunications began on May 19, 1933, (11) Shanghai-London, telecommunications scheduled to begin on February 3, 1934.

Chairman of Guangxi Province Huang Xuchu Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 117

Scheduled to Take a Ship to Hong Kong Tomorrow to Return to Guangxi

Mr. Chen Talks About Guangxi Province's Efforts in Construction

Huang Xuchu, a member of the Central Committee and Chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government, came to Shanghai from Guangxi to attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee in Nanjing. A reporter from the Xinxin News Agency made a special visit yesterday to inquire about everything. This is because the total annual revenue of Guangxi Province's entire finances is only about 20 million yuan. Fortunately, the expenses of the military and government are very light (the total annual expenditure in the budget is about 10 million). This is because there are very few troops. The total number of provincial troops is currently about 45,000, plus about 7,000 to 8,000 militia, totaling less than 60,000. Moreover, a part of them is still assisting the Central Army in suppressing bandits in Jiangxi, so the supply is still low. Therefore, the Guangxi authorities have used all of the financial revenue except for expenses for construction in recent years. Furthermore, the banditry in Guangxi Province has now been completely eliminated, and the people can live and work in peace.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to Request That the Salt Weight Be Changed Without Increasing Taxes 122

Calculate the Proportion According to the Municipal Weight

Avoid the Policy of Increasing Taxes by Changing the System

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying: "To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 31st of this month, we received a telegram from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which read: 'To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission: Since the Hubei Salt Affairs Inspection Office announced that the salt weight would be changed to the municipal weight and the tax rate would remain the same, the grocery and liquor industries have repeatedly requested that the tax rate be reduced according to the municipal weight to alleviate the people's difficulties. It is true that changing the salt weight to the municipal weight and unifying the measurement rules is necessary for government decrees. However, the new municipal weight system requires 124 catties to be equivalent to 100 catties of the old weight. The tax rate for salt should be calculated and reduced according to the percentage ratio to be fair. Now that the measuring instruments have been updated but the tax rate remains the same, 100 catties of salt under the new weight will have to pay the same tax as 100 catties of the old weight. According to secret calculations, the tax rate for every 100 catties of salt has suddenly increased by more than 24 percent. It is called changing the weight, but in reality, it is increasing the tax. This is probably not the original intention of the government to protect the people. We believe that the Central Committee and Chairman Chiang are doing everything possible to help the rural areas. At a time when the rural areas are bankrupt and the people's livelihood is deteriorating, how can they bear this heavy tax? Moreover, salt is a necessity for the lives of ordinary people, and the sales volume in rural areas is particularly large. The so-called salt tax is actually a poll tax. If the governing officials give a little consideration to this policy of increasing taxes on a per capita basis, they will not be willing to do it. Salt is related to the people's livelihood, and it is not convenient to suppress it. We beg you to look into the situation and allow the weight to be changed without increasing taxes, which will benefit the people without costing anything. We will be grateful beyond measure. We are anxiously awaiting your orders.' The Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows to you." It has been found that changing the salt weight to the municipal weight and secretly increasing taxes is close to deceiving the people and has a profound and significant impact on the people's livelihood. We hope that we can strive for a consistent approach and strive to achieve the goal of changing the weight without increasing taxes. We are anxiously awaiting your orders. We approve of this and find that Hubei salt must use the municipal weight, but the tax rate is still collected according to the old rate, which invisibly increases the burden on salt merchants. The people who are directly affected are still the ordinary people. It is appropriate to report the situation and ask the Ministry to examine and approve it, and to allow the tax amount to be corrected proportionally according to the number converted by the municipal weight, so as to avoid the name of unifying the measurement system and secretly increasing taxes, which is truly fair and convenient. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows to you.

Page 13

The River Level Continues to Drop to Eight Feet Nine Inches 123

A Rare New Record in Decades

Bombing Reefs to Save the Emei

The interruption of navigation on the Yangtze River due to shallow water, which hinders the passage of ships up and down the river, has been reported in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, the river level has continued to recede in recent days, and the discovery of an even shallower water level yesterday is a rare occurrence in recent decades. The record is as follows:

Water Level Continues to Decrease 124

On Monday and Tuesday of this week, the water level in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River dropped sharply. Between Xiaogushan and Madang, the shortest time it dropped to was nine feet two inches. All ships used barges, resulting in many ships being stopped up and down Madang. Unexpectedly, on Wednesday night, the water level at that location dropped again. After verification by the Jianghan Customs, it dropped another three inches. Since yesterday, the Yangtze River water has been found to have the shallowest record of eight feet nine inches.

Night Navigation Prohibited 125

Yesterday, the Jianghan Customs issued another notice stating that the water level from Jiujiang up to Hankou is eleven feet and zero inches, while from Jiujiang down to Wuhu, it is only eight feet and nine inches. Effective immediately, the river surface between Madang is not suitable for ships with shallow draft and night navigation is prohibited to avoid danger. The local Nisshin Kisen Kaisha has already suspended the voyage of the "Luoyang Maru" because of its large size and deep draft. They have reassigned the "Zuiyo Maru," which has the shallowest draft, to operate in order to prevent grounding.

The Difficult Rescue of Changxing 126

The "Changxing" steamer of the Sanbei Company has been aground at Madang for five days. First, the "Yongkang," "Sanbei," and "Fuyang" steamers were sent to tow it, but all failed to dislodge it. Next, the "Awakened Lion" was dispatched to pull it, but it was also unable to rescue it because it was deeply embedded in the sand and mud. A ship has now been sent to unload the cargo from all the cabins before attempting another rescue. Yesterday, according to a telegram from the owner of the steamer, it is still difficult to free it. There is little hope of pulling it off the shoal within a week.

The Four Hongs Retreat to Hankou 127

In the upper reaches of the Yangtze, the water level at Xindi is the shallowest, having risen from four and a half feet to five and a half feet. However, unexpectedly, the river water there dropped again after Tuesday of this week, receding five inches, leaving only five feet of water. The ships traveling up and down the river, waiting for the water to rise before proceeding, were once again disappointed. Except for smaller ships that could be lightered and towed, the "Hongyuan," "Hongheng," "Hongzhen," and "Hongli," the four ships of Sanbei, fully loaded with salt from Juan, were all blocked at Xindi. Later, they retreated to the Luoshan river surface to anchor. Now, Mr. Song, the general manager of Juan, has personally gone to inspect the area. Fearing bandit activity in the Luoshan area, he agreed with Sanbei to have all the salt on the four Hong ships returned to Hankou for anchorage, awaiting a rise in water before proceeding to Changsha.

Blasting Reefs for the Emei 128

The China Merchants Bureau's upper Yangtze steamer "Emei" ran aground on a reef at Huatanzi in Fuzhou in July of last year. The entire ship was damaged by the raging torrents of the Sichuan River. Repair costs have already reached 100,000 yuan. Now, with the water in the upper Yangtze greatly receding, the "Emei" is even more aground on the rocks along the bank, at a distance of several dozen feet from the surface of the Sichuan River. Taking advantage of this excellent opportunity, the China Merchants Bureau decided to use explosives to blast all the reefs under the ship's hull, destroying the rocks and moving the ship's hull downward. Once the spring waters rise, it can be towed away. This matter has been telegraphed to Ouyang Baida, the director of the Yichang branch, who is responsible for handling it. A total of 5,000 yuan will be spent. The explosives have been transported there. Yesterday, a telegram was received from Yichang stating that the blasting of the reefs had begun. It is estimated that within a week, all the reefs under the ship's hull can be blasted away.
