Match Manufacturers Request Relief 138

The match manufacturers in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces feel that the sudden increase in heavy taxes by the Ministry of Finance is too difficult to bear. Therefore, they have been meeting in Shanghai for several days to discuss relief measures. Those who attended included Gao Songfu and Dong Junchen, representatives from the Shanghai Dahua Factory; Sun Runzhai and Shen Qixiang, representatives from the China Factory; Xu Jingzhi and Hu Zenan, representatives from the Ningbo Zhengda Factory; Xu Guangji, a representative from the Linhuai Huaishang Factory; Yao Baozhen, a representative from the Wenzhou Suichang Factory; Chen Chaozhong, a representative from the Nantong Tongsui Factory; Shao Xiushan, a representative from the Shanghai Daming Factory; and Cai Keming, a representative from the Shanghai Huaming Factory, totaling more than twenty people. After two days of meetings, they decided to organize the Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Anhui Match Industry Advancement Association, with a preparatory office located at No. 3, Alley 10, Intersection of Fuzhou Road and Shanxi Road in Shanghai. Gao Songfu, Sun Runzhai, and seven others were elected as preparatory members. They also decided that the manufacturers from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui would jointly petition the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Executive Yuan, the Central Party Headquarters, and other agencies, requesting a reduction in taxes and measures for relief. The petition listed the various hardships suffered by the factories and four methods of seeking relief. The main point was that after the sudden increase in heavy taxes, including the original tax amount, it accounts for about 70% of the cost of goods. The economic burden is difficult to bear, the use of capital is even more insufficient, there are too many old labels, new goods are difficult to sell, and the work in each factory will inevitably be suspended, with workers facing unemployment. Therefore, they requested a reduction in tax rates, a limited sale of old labels, restrictions on the establishment of factories, and incentives for artificial manufacturing, etc., in order to provide relief and maintain them. It is reported that, in addition to submitting written petitions to the party and government agencies, the manufacturers are also seeking solidarity and mutual assistance, aiming to cooperate and actively preparing for the advancement association. They also support the National Match Industry Joint Association as the national leader.

The Red Swastika Society Handles Emergency Relief in Changyuan 139

The Tragic Disaster of Ice Jams on the Yellow River

The World Red Swastika Society previously dispatched relief team leader Yu Yuanguan to Changyuan to distribute winter relief. A letter has now been received from Changyuan reporting that the county is currently suffering another major calamity due to ice jams on the Yellow River. Over thirty villages along both banks of the river have been washed away by the water. The depth of the water is over ten feet in some places and several feet in others. Countless people and animals have frozen to death. The situation is extremely serious, and relief efforts are also difficult. In addition to the team actively working hard to rescue the victims, the original letter is copied below, hoping that philanthropists at home and abroad will provide more assistance. This is a report of the matter. Investigations revealed that the breaches on both the east and west banks of the Yellow River last year were both within Changyuan County. The severity of the disaster was the worst among the counties in other provinces. Currently, the national and provincial governments and various charitable organizations have provided multiple emergency and winter relief efforts, and the villagers have gradually returned home to build earthen shelters and temporary dwellings. Unexpectedly, due to the excessive ice jams in Hua County, ice water overflowed suddenly on the evening of January 13th, flowing from north to south and horizontally breaching the villages along the new river channel, including Zhangzhuang, Sanniangzhai, Fangliji, Dasuzhuang, Xiaosuzhuang, Zhaituan, Sanguanmiao, Sulu Village, Dongdenggang, Wangzhuang, Lizhai, Getang, Yuanzhai, Liuzhuang, Zhaizhai, Xingzhai, Zhaozhai, Leidian, Tianzhuang, Cuizhai, Yangzhai, various Shitouzhai, Zhihuzhai, Lizhuang, Dalizhai, Chenzhai, Xiasai, Guosai, Lizhai, Sunlou, and Jiujiji, totaling thirty-eight villages. Even the Iron Furnace Village of Zhishi, which resisted bandits led by Ji Qi, was broken open by the ice, with water depths of over ten feet in some places and several feet in others. Those who could not escape in time, without boats or vehicles to cross the ice, had their toes broken and skin torn. Those clinging to buildings and trees were pierced by the cold wind. Cries for help could be heard for several miles. Countless houses were submerged and collapsed, and countless people and animals froze, starved, and drowned. The severity of the disaster is ten times worse than the breaches in autumn and summer. Currently, team members are actively rescuing the victims. Those who have been rescued from the water are given relief food. Efforts are also being made to rescue those still in the water, etc.

New Province Airmail Temporarily Suspended 140

Non-Airmail Items Can Still Be Accepted

The Shanghai Postal Administration issued a notice yesterday stating that the Xinjiang postal route has been completely blocked, and mail communication has been suspended. Various types of mail to Xinjiang that were previously accepted by the post office are currently temporarily suspended and cannot be delivered. Except for Xinjiang airmail that must be transported via the Gansu-Jiuquan west-bound route, which should be temporarily suspended from acceptance, the post office can still accept other non-airmail items to Xinjiang and transport them to the blocked location first. Once the postal route is restored, they will be forwarded immediately. This notice is hereby issued for public information.

New Initiatives After the Reorganization of the Cotton Cloth Market 142

The Chinese National Cotton Cloth Market on Guizhou Road in Shanghai was initiated by Zhang Zilian and others. After the reorganization, Du Yuesheng became the chairman and Zhang Rongchu became the general manager. The subscribed capital of 250,000 yuan has been fully paid, and business has begun. Buying machine-woven cloth with cash during this crucial period of year-end settlement for the business community is especially beneficial to small industrial and commercial enterprises. It is reported that the market plans to provide pure domestic yarn to machine weavers in the future. The market will purchase the woven cloth and then sell it. The Railway Business Office Appropriately Reduces the Freight Receiving and Delivery Fees 143

Effective Today

The Shanghai General Business Office of the Two Railways, in order to facilitate merchants, specially signed thirteen provisional measures with the Taiping Moving Company for the receiving and delivery of goods, which were submitted to the railway bureau for approval and implementation. As the measures were not comprehensive enough and the set rates for receiving and delivery were also considered slightly high, the business office further negotiated with the company to appropriately reduce the receiving and delivery fees and added five additional articles, all of which will be implemented starting today. The original text of the additional articles is as follows: (1) For each household whose goods weigh less than one metric ton, the business office will handle the receiving and delivery itself. Only for goods weighing one metric ton or more will the company be entrusted to dispatch a vehicle for receiving and delivery. (2) The company agrees to revise the freight receiving and delivery fees as follows: First and second class freight: 25 cents of silver per 100 kilograms (originally 30 cents); Third and fourth class freight: 20 cents of silver per 100 kilograms (originally 25 cents); Fifth and sixth class freight: 15 cents of silver per 100 kilograms (originally 20 cents). The above weight will still be calculated based on the railway's chargeable weight, with no minimum weight requirement. (3) For the delivery of soap from the China Soap Company by vehicle, a receiving fee of one yuan and five jiao of silver per ton will be charged, and the company will be paid at a 95% discount. (4) The fees for receiving and delivering coffins or empty caskets are as follows: One item: 6 yuan; Two items: 8 yuan; Three items: 10.5 yuan; Four items: 12 yuan; Five items: 14 yuan; Six items: 15 yuan (originally a flat rate of 6 yuan per item). The above receiving and delivery fees will be paid to the company at a 90% discount. (5) All provisions in the provisional measures that do not conflict with this annex remain valid.

Annual Work Report of the Shanghai Municipal Police 144

Cars Increased by 42% in Five Years

Six Kidnapping Cases Occurred in the Concession This Year

Major Jarrad, Commissioner of the Shanghai Municipal Police, reported on the past year's work, stating that there were a total of 32 encounters between patrolling police and armed bandits during the year, resulting in one police officer killed and eight injured. Eleven bandits were killed and thirteen injured. The discipline and integrity of all police personnel were excellent. The General Reserve Unit and Special Police were also extremely effective.

Traffic Problems: The increasing number of vehicles of all kinds has made it increasingly difficult for the police to manage traffic. The number of cars alone has increased by 42% in five years. The narrow streets and the parking of vehicles often obstruct traffic. The situation has improved since the opening of the Race Course Road, but the road has not been fully utilized. The one-way traffic rule has been implemented on Hong Kong Road and Sichuan Road with good results. Traffic lights have been installed at 68 intersections, and there are plans to test an electric lighting system in the future. The motorcycle patrol team has been quite effective. A total of 53,034 traffic violations were recorded this year, of which 8,495 were prosecuted (7,845 Chinese and 650 foreigners). 16,249 car drivers were registered. 386 people were prosecuted for honking excessively. There are 107 electric trams and 107 trailer cars. The total number of passengers for the year was 119,669,536. There are 164 buses and 1,656 freight cars. Four vehicles were scrapped due to damage, and 173 licenses were revoked due to damage. There are currently 47 taxi companies with 44 more taxis. Licenses were revoked for 19 vehicles due to unsanitary conditions. There are currently 9,990 licensed public rickshaws, which are inspected every two months. 26,571 cases of rickshaw pullers being prosecuted for violations in the Central and Old Zha districts were recorded. The average number of licenses issued for private rickshaws per quarter was 12,579, an increase of 1,321 from the previous year. Strict measures have been taken to crack down on the unauthorized soliciting of passengers, which has been greatly reduced. 29,242 bicycles were registered, with an average of 13,242 flatbed carts and 8,841 handcarts. These heavy vehicles are still able to compete with cars due to their low cost. There are currently 32 horse-drawn carriage companies with 100 carriages. They are rarely used except for weddings and funerals.

Traffic Accidents: Statistics for the past five years are as follows: 9,691 cases in 1929, with 3,447 injuries and 141 deaths; 10,973 cases in 1930, with 4,005 injuries and 142 deaths; 12,948 cases in 1931, with 4,570 injuries and 143 deaths; 12,016 cases in 1932, with 4,250 injuries and 134 deaths; 13,571 cases in 1933, with 4,495 injuries and 107 deaths. Although the number of cases has increased, the number of deaths has decreased. The ages of the deceased last year were: 2 were under 5 years old, 31 were between 5 and 15 years old, 50 were between 15 and 40 years old, and 24 were over 40 years old. The number of cars in the concession last year was 5,756 private cars, 1,013 public cars, 1,656 freight cars, 162 buses, and 717 motorcycles. In addition, 63 commercial licenses were issued.

Communication Methods: The police department implemented a centralized traffic agency, which has proven to be effective. Recently, teleprinters have been added for further convenience. The headquarters' radio broadcasting has been quite effective. However, the radio patrol cars need to be replaced with new ones.

Number of Crimes: According to the report, there were 1 case this year, and there were 4,927 unsolved cases at the end of the year. 24,513 criminals were arrested this year. Excluding those who have been released and those who are still in custody, 22,412 were convicted by the court after trial.

Kidnapping Cases: There were six kidnapping cases this year and two attempted kidnappings (eleven kidnapping cases in 1932, with three attempted; seventeen kidnapping cases in 1931, with eight attempted; thirty-three kidnapping cases in 1930, with three attempted). Two hostages were rescued by police in the concession, two were redeemed by themselves, and the whereabouts of the other two hostages are still unknown. One hostage was hidden in this concession, two were hidden in the French Concession, one was hidden in the Chinese territory, and the whereabouts of the other two are unknown. Five of the six cases involved cars. Two were cars owned by the car owner, and three were cars prepared by the kidnappers themselves. 128 cases of receiving threatening letters were recorded this year (174 cases in 1932, 183 cases in 1931, and 228 cases in 1930). As a result, 40 people were arrested, and 34 have been sentenced.

Property Theft: There were 443 armed robbery cases (504 cases last year, 529 cases the year before, and 702 cases the year before that). There were 105 other robbery cases. The total value of stolen property this year was 1,307,994 yuan (2,184,313 yuan last year, and 5,850,741 yuan the year before that). Recovered property totaled 427,879 yuan, accounting for 32.71%. It was found that embezzled and fraudulent property accounted for 433,157 yuan, accounting for over 33%, which can be regarded as something that the police cannot prevent.

Fingerprint Work: The fingerprint section received 32,723 fingerprint cards throughout the year. Of these, 10,667 were found to be recidivists. 10,663 criminal fingerprints were transferred to the French Concession Police Department.

Identification of Firearms: The Firearms Identification Section identified 369 fired and unfired bullets and 285 firearms this year. Identified firearms used by criminals accounted for 15%. 40% of the seized firearms were from Spain, 19% from France, 18% from Germany, 9% from Belgium, 6% from the United States, and the rest from Italy, Japan, Austria, and other countries.

Communist Activities: In addition to attempting demonstrations and distributing propaganda and posting slogans among workers, communist elements also planned assassination activities this year. The police department cooperated with the Chinese authorities and discovered 174 organizations, arresting 223 people. Of these, 91 were handed over to the Chinese authorities (including five who had already been sentenced to death), one was handed over to the French Concession, five were handed over to consulates, 34 were sentenced by the court within the concession, and 91 were released on bail. One person was in custody pending trial at the end of the year. A total of 338 types of communist documents were seized, totaling 71,607 copies.

Labor Problems: There were 63 strikes in the concession this year, affecting 22,613 workers, with a loss of 202,171 workdays. Of these, 25 strikes were unconditionally resumed, 15 strikes resulted in slight gains for the workers, 14 strikes were completely resolved to the satisfaction of the workers, and the remaining 9 strikes had no definite outcome. 15 strikes were mediated by a third party. 32 factories were closed due to strikes. 19,631 workers were unemployed. Of these, 17 were later reopened, and 13,715 workers were re-employed.

Page 14

Li Minzhou, General Manager of the New-New Company, Assassinated Last Night 145

Li Had Only Succeeded to the Position of General Manager for Just Over a Year

Last Night He Was on the Third Floor of the Hotel, About to Take a Bath

The Assailant Took Advantage of the Opportunity to Break in and Shot Li Twice

Li Died Immediately, and the Police Dispatched Detectives to Investigate

｜The Assailant Was Zhou Zhanyuan, the Head of the Gatekeepers of the New-New Company｜

Li Minzhou, the general manager of the New-New Department Store on Nanjing Road and Guizhou Road, was shot and killed by Zhou Zhanyuan, the head of the gatekeepers, at 6:30 PM yesterday in the general manager's office on the third floor of the New-New Hotel. The bullets hit vital points, causing his immediate death. The details are recorded below. He succeeded as general manager when the New-New Company reached its eighth-anniversary celebration. When Liu Xiji was the general manager, Li Minzhou was the manager. After Liu passed away due to illness, Li was elected as general manager by the board of directors and had been in the position for over a year. He was extremely capable and had a great work ethic.

Removing Clothes to Bathe

Yesterday at approximately 6:30 PM, after finishing his work in the company office, Li walked into the general manager's office, room 327 on the third floor of the New-New Hotel. He took off his outer robe and had just leaned against the sofa when Guan Yizhang (age 28, Cantonese), a servant from room 37, entered to serve him. Li then instructed Guan Yizhang to go to the inner bathroom to run water. As Li was taking off his shoes and socks on the sofa, the assailant took advantage of the opportunity to break in.

Two Shots Struck Him

Suddenly, a robust man, Zhou Zhanyuan from Tianjin, wearing the uniform of the company's gatekeepers, barged into the room. Without saying a word, he raised his gun and shot Li twice. One bullet hit near the left breast, piercing through the back, and the other hit the left waist, but did not exit. Seeing that his goal had been achieved, the assailant fled the room and rushed down the stairs. At that moment, Li cried out for help. Guan Yizhang, the servant in the bathroom, heard the gunshots followed by Li's groans. He rushed out and helped Li to the residence of his relative, a Mr. Chen, in room 305. However, Li was severely wounded and collapsed by the bed, dying soon after.

Upon hearing the bad news, the tea room staff on the third floor immediately notified the accounting room below by telephone and quickly closed the main gate to pursue the assailant. They also reported to the Laozha Police Station, and the police chief immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives, armed, to search for him. Unfortunately, the assailant had already vanished. Shortly after, an ambulance arrived and rushed Li to Renji Hospital. Doctors performed surgery and administered strong heart stimulants, but Li's injuries were too severe, and he died within ten minutes.

The Assailant Arrested

When the detectives investigated, they found a bullet on the sofa in room 327, which they took to the police station as evidence. It is said that the police are taking this case very seriously. After the incident, they ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to search for the assailant everywhere. At around 10:00 PM, the detectives captured the suspect and detained him at the police station. This morning, he was sent to the court for investigation.

Li's Family Background 146

Li Minzhou was from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province, and was 53 years old. He had some assets and lived in a Western-style house at 202 Bazi Road. His wife, Gao, was over 40 years old, and they had four children. The eldest son, Renru, was 17 years old and studied at the Guangdong Public School in Zhabei.

Reason for the Assassination 147

The assailant, Zhou Zhanyuan, was from Tianjin and was 45 years old. He was hired from the north as a gatekeeper when the New-New Company opened. Because he was diligent in his duties, he was later promoted to head of the gatekeepers, a position he had held for several years. Recently, the company authorities, considering the position of head of the gatekeepers to be unimportant, dismissed him just yesterday. Zhou, having suffered this unexpected blow and facing an uncertain future, expressed dissatisfaction with the general manager and resolutely took this drastic action, going to assassinate him.

Massive Fraud Case at the Banque de l'Indochine Involving Chinese, English, Italian, and Russian Individuals 148

English and Italian Perpetrators Handed Over to Their Respective Consulates

Chinese and Russian Perpetrators Interrogated Yesterday by the Special Court No. 1

Ten Chinese and Foreign Individuals Appeared in Court to Testify

British Consulate Police Court Summoned Englishman Mark Yesterday

Following the revelation of a massive fraud at the Banque de l'Indochine, involving a sum of 136,818.50 yuan, the Public Concession Police Department launched an investigation, gradually apprehending over ten suspects of Chinese, English, Italian, and Russian nationalities. Except for the English and Italian perpetrators, who enjoyed consular jurisdiction and were handed over to their respective consulates for investigation, the two Russian nationals, Joussoupov Aharonovich Smaransky and Tzein, and the two Chinese nationals, Wang Chunggan (aka Wang Haoran) and Xie Pingfeng, were prosecuted by the Shanghai Municipal Council's lawyers, Ru Bao-yi and Li Zhi-shan, on charges of fraud, forgery, counterfeiting documents, and using forged documents, etc., at the First Special District Court, which was reported in the newspapers.

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qian Hongye of the Criminal Division No. 1 specially convened a hearing, ordering the four defendants to be brought before the court for interrogation. Many Russian expatriates in Shanghai attended the hearing. The two Russian defendants were defended by Lawyer Phipps, Wang Chunggan was defended by Lawyer Mao Xianshen, and Lawyers Zhang Chongding, Fan Gang, and Wang Jian represented Xie Pingfeng.

First, SMC Lawyer Ru Bao-yi gave a detailed account of the police's investigation process and the legal basis for the prosecution, explaining the fraudulent scheme of forging fake checks from the British American Tobacco Company and using the Guohua Bank to cash them at the Banque de l'Indochine for over 130,000 yuan, which was the same as previously reported. Therefore, we will not repeat it here. However, how this huge sum was divided is still unknown to the outside world. According to Lawyer Ru, based on the police investigation, and limited to the four defendants on trial at the Special Court, the first defendant, Joussoupov Aharonovich, received 44,000 yuan, the second defendant received 4,500 yuan, and the fourth defendant received 5,500 yuan. The exact amount received by the third defendant is still unclear.

Lawyer Ru continued to explain the method used by the group to steal checks that had already been cashed by the British American Tobacco Company from the Banque de l'Indochine in order to forge the fake checks. The second defendant, Wang Chunggan, was an employee of the Banque de l'Indochine. He, at the request of the first defendant, stole two checks that had already been cashed by the British American Tobacco Company from the vault and handed them over to the first defendant. The first defendant then instructed the third defendant to have the checks photographed and a copper plate made. The printing was then done, and a sum of over 130,000 yuan was filled in, falsely claiming it was paid to the China Tobacco Leaf Company. There is no such company in Shanghai, but there are such companies in the North and Qingdao. After the name of the company was created, a mailbox was rented at the post office to receive any correspondence.

After the Banque de l'Indochine cashed the check, the forged check was originally to be kept, but it was unexpectedly torn up, leaving only a corner. It was exactly the same as the second forged check for over 180,000 yuan created by the group. Thus, the format of the first check could be imagined from the color and shape of the second fake check. Lawyer Ru concluded by stating that the Englishman Mark, who guaranteed the opening of accounts at Guohua Bank and other banks in the names of the defendants, had already been prosecuted by the Shanghai Municipal Council at the British Consulate. In addition, an accomplice, a Russian man with a missing finger, has been apprehended in Tianjin and will soon be escorted to Shanghai for trial.

Judge Qian then began to question the witnesses. A total of ten people appeared in court to testify. They were two employees of the British American Tobacco Company, Englishman Wilbur and Cowdery, who testified that the checks issued by the British American Tobacco Company required their signatures and that the signatures on the forged checks were not theirs. They also said that the fake checks were so accurately imitated that it was difficult to distinguish the genuine from the fake at first glance. Next was an Englishman, an accountant at the Banque de l'Indochine, who testified about the discovery of the fake checks, stating that the British American Tobacco Company checks were issued by the bank. Because the numbers on the fake checks did not match, it was known that they were fake. According to regulations, all checks that have been paid are stored in a room, and all bank employees have free access to the room. Wang Chunggan, as a bank employee, could also enter the room.

The fourth witness was Russian, Coxinin, who testified about the first defendant opening an account at Guohua Bank and Shanghai Bank in the name of the China Tobacco Leaf Company. He said that he had known the first defendant for six years and that opening accounts at both banks was entrusted to him. First, the application form was filled out, and the first defendant asked Mark to guarantee it, and the seal of Chinese Li Wenzhun was affixed to the application form, and submitted to the two banks for approval. After the approval, the first defendant deposited 1,050 yuan in cash to the Shanghai Bank through him, and 700-800 yuan by check and 100 yuan in cash to the Guohua Bank, all in the name of China Tobacco Leaf Company.

The witness following Coxinin was also a Russian photographer, Lefjevski, who claimed that in July or August of last year, the first defendant ordered him to photograph two checks from the British American Tobacco Company to the Banque de l'Indochine, without specifying the purpose. However, he was instructed to keep it a secret. Between January 17 and 18 of this year, when he went to Mark's company to collect money from the first defendant, he saw a check for over 180,000 yuan, and Mark was affixing Li Wenzhun's seal on the back of the check.

The testimony of the witness was quite different from his statement at the police station, but he admitted in court that the statement presented by the police was in his handwriting. After that, two Japanese photographers and printers testified one after another. One specially certified that the copper plate was made for a Russian with a missing finger (the one arrested in Tianjin), and the other specially certified that after the copper plate was made, the Japanese photographer accompanied the Russian with a missing finger to the printing factory he had set up on Zhapu Road, where the Russian with a missing finger took out the copper plate and the paper he had brought and ordered him to print the copper plate on the paper, and the Russian with a missing finger took it away after printing.

At this point, Lawyer Ru stood up and stated that before asking the Japanese to make the plate and print, the group had asked the Da Zhonghua Printing Factory to undertake this work, but because the factory's technology was not good, it was abandoned even after the work was completed, so they turned to the Japanese for it. So, Chen, the director of Da Zhonghua, came to court to testify about the circumstances of the first and third defendants, Russian, coming to the factory to make plates and print. Also, Russian Fantaulof testified that the first defendant asked him to rent a mailbox at the post office on his behalf. Finally, two employees, Jiang and Xia, of the Huamei Engraving Shop testified about the facts that the first and third defendants came to the shop to order the printing of stationery and envelopes for the China Tobacco Leaf Company and the engraving of rubber stamps.

After more than five hours of testimony, the court adjourned and announced that the hearing would be continued on another day. The four defendants were returned to custody.

Interrogation of Mark: The North-China Daily News reports that Englishman Mark, accused of conspiring with Russian Ivanov and others to use fake checks to defraud the Banque de l'Indochine of 136,688.25 yuan, was further tried in the British Consulate Police Court yesterday. The prosecuting attorney, McLair, stated that he was not prepared to proceed with the case at this time because the important evidence was all in the First Special District Court, used to try Ivanov. If Ivanov is innocent, the case can be completed in one or two days, so please extend the hearing.

Next, the defendant's lawyer, Harup, requested bail on behalf of the defendant, saying that the previous application was not approved because it was feared that the release of the person concerned would hinder the police's investigation. Now that the police investigation has been completed, there is no need to worry about this. The presiding judge then ordered the defendant to provide bail of 2,500 yuan, and two more Englishmen to each guarantee 2,500 yuan for his release. The defendant's passport should be temporarily deposited with the registry. The next hearing is scheduled for 10:30 AM on February 9.

Russian Teenager Commits Suicide in the Yangtze Hotel 149

Shoots Himself in the Heart with a Pistol

Seriously Wounded, Life in Danger

At the Yangtze Hotel on Sanma Road at about 10 AM yesterday, a Russian teenager suddenly came with a pistol at his waist and went to room 722 on the seventh floor of the hotel. He paid 3.80 yuan for the room, gave 4 yuan, and asked the tea room attendant to get envelopes and stationery, wrote a letter in Western language, and instructed the tea room attendant to send it immediately to his office at the China Business Company on Sichuan Road, Sanma Road. After speaking, the Russian teenager raised his own pistol and fired a shot at his chest. The bullet entered his heart, blood flowed profusely, and he collapsed to the ground. Truth Revealed About the Tragic Death of an Apprentice at the Shanghai Municipal Council Hygiene Department's Laboratory 150

The Injury Behind the Head Was Definitely Sustained While Alive

Death Was Caused by Taking Poison After the Injury

Shi Shaoxing, an apprentice at Xu Futai Western Clothing Store on Dalianwan Road, died under unclear circumstances. Prosecutor Guo of the First Special District Court had ordered the injured part of the deceased's back of the head to be sent to a doctor for a chemical test to determine the cause of death, pending his report for verification. Shi Qixiang, the uncle of the deceased, believed that he was killed by the shop owner, Xu Futai, and his wife, Xu Chen. He had retained Lawyer Wu Peng to file a criminal complaint against the Xu couple for cruel murder. The court had also summoned them once. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper.

It is now known that after the Special Court handed over the injured limbs of the deceased to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Hygiene Department, a Western doctor with experience at the department conducted a thorough chemical test using various techniques. It was confirmed that the injury behind the head was definitely sustained while alive, but the extent of the injury was not fatal. Therefore, the cause of death was further studied. As a result of the examination, it was determined that after being injured, the deceased had taken poison similar to opium, resulting in his death. The details of the chemical test and the results obtained were written in a detailed report and submitted to the court for verification.

This chaotic murder case, which lasted for two weeks, finally revealed the cause of death. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo announced the report at the autopsy site. Lawyer Wu Peng, the representative of the deceased's family, was also present. The defendants, Xu Futai and his wife, were both summoned but did not arrive. Xu himself had requested to surrender for interrogation after being accused. It is now heard that he has retained Lawyer Chen Tingrui to act as his defense. Presumably, when the Special Court opens this case, the defendant will appear in court with his lawyer.

Impersonating a Detective, Planting Evidence, and Extorting Money Will Ultimately Not Escape the Grasp of the Law 151

Chen Songhe Encountered an Accident While Saying Goodbye

A Pistol and Bullets Were Stuffed into His Bed

Resulting in Paying 700 Yuan to Buy His Way Out

Chen Took the Original Steamer Back to Shanghai to Report to the Police

Chen Songhe, a native of Ningbo, currently 39 years old, residing at 1002 Broadway Road, East Head of the Public Concession, owns and operates a Maolin Hardware and Sail Shop, possesses some assets, and uses a car for transportation. He is friendly with Shen Zihuai, a fellow villager residing at No. 8 Ningfu Lane, Grek Road, French Concession. On the afternoon of the 27th of last month, Chen planned to return to his hometown on the New Jiangtian Steamer. He first drove his own car to Shen Zihuai's home at 3 o'clock to say goodbye, and then went to the pier to depart.

Chen arrived at Shen's house and talked for about thirty minutes. Hu Quanhai (age 40, residing at No. 7 Huabao Lane, Huanghe Road, French Concession, a few hundred steps away from Shen Zihuai's residence), a fellow villager known to Chen, led three accomplices (unknown to Chen) into Shen Zihuai's home, claiming to search for red pills. They dragged Chen, Shen, and Shen's family from the living room to the room behind the living room, pretending to search everywhere. The group took the opportunity to stuff a pistol and a box of bullets containing about a hundred bullets into the bed. At that time, Chen was standing next to the bed, so they pretended to find the gun and bullets, and asked Chen where he got this prohibited military material. Chen was dumbfounded and could not answer.

At this time, an accomplice who came with Hu, claiming to be surnamed Jiang, spoke with a Northern accent, drew a pistol and threatened him, forbidding him to publicize. Another man, claiming to be surnamed Wang, reached out and handcuffed Chen's hands. Hu and others then began to negotiate, saying that extorting money could resolve the matter and make it go away. The man surnamed Jiang asked Shen Zihuai's wife if she knew old friends, and asked if she knew Jin Tingsheng. Shen's wife replied that she did not know him. Jiang then mentioned Bao Songqing (age 50, a native of Ningbo, residing at No. 5 Yong'an Lane, Beir Road, French Concession), asking if she knew him. She replied that she knew him slightly, so someone was sent to invite Bao over to negotiate extortion with Chen Songhe.

While threatening him with words, after some deliberation, Chen, because he was anxious to return to his hometown and was threatened, had no choice but to agree to pay 700 yuan to settle the crime of privately possessing military material. After the two parties reached an agreement, they forced Chen to sign a check for 700 yuan payable immediately from Hengli Bank before Chen's handcuffs were removed. The man surnamed Jiang escorted Chen in Chen's car to Hengli Bank to withdraw cash, and then they returned to Shen's home together. After the money was handed over to Bao Songqing, Jiang escorted Chen to the New Jiangtian Steamer. When he arrived at the pier, the steamer was already raising anchor and leaving, so Jiang sent Chen onto the steamer, watched the steamer leave the dock and sail out, and then ordered the driver in Chen's car to drive to the front of the French Concession Xiafei Road, Songshan Road Police Station. Jiang told the driver, "I am a special detective here." After saying that, he left.

The driver then drove the car back to the owner's house and told the mistress what happened to the owner. But when Chen Songhe boarded the ship, the ship had already sailed, and he could not disembark, so he had to go to Ningbo on the steamer and then return to Shanghai on the original steamer to report to the French Concession Police Station, requesting an investigation. The police chief sent detectives to investigate and only arrested Bao Songqing. The others, such as Hu Quanhai and his three accomplices, had heard the news and fled, and could not be arrested. Bao was taken to the police station and sent to the Criminal Division No. 1 of the Second Special District Court yesterday morning. Judge Wang Gangxu conducted the trial. The police lawyer, Gu Shouxi, stated the case, briefly stating that the defendant was arrested for the crime of extortion and fraud. Because the police have not yet investigated and the accomplices are still at large, he requested a postponement, and temporarily detain the defendant, pending investigation of the details of the case and the arrest of the accomplices, and requested a trial.

Next, the plaintiff Chen Songhe testified about the defendant's extortion. After briefly questioning Bao Songqing, the court ordered a postponement of the hearing to February 5. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Both Criminal Law and Regulations Violated: Evil Pimp Forces Good Women into Prostitution 152

Ye Jinfeng Was Induced to Come to Shanghai and Sold into a Brothel

Tang Chen Constantly Uses Her Power to Force Women to Work

Ye Jinfeng, a woman from Liyang, is 22 years old and not yet married. She had an affair with Tang Dafu (also known as Fugeng) from her hometown. On the seventh day of the fifth lunar month of last year, she was brought to Shanghai by Tang and forced into the brothel opened by Tang Chen, a Jiangbei woman, at No. 4 Jinyu Lane, Zhujia Bridge, French Concession, as a prostitute. At that time, a contract was signed for a term of four years, with an annual deposit of 53 yuan. Tang took 110 yuan in advance, and the rest would be paid after she completed her term. However, the woman was only told that it would be for a term of one year. The woman was illiterate and was deceived into signing the deposit contract.

When the one-year term expired, the woman wanted to leave the brothel and return home, but the madam refused to let her go. She did not specify a term and used her power. The woman was alone in Shanghai, helpless, and had to endure the pain. Now, half a year has passed. Recently, the woman could not bear the physical pain and vowed to escape the misery, so she took the opportunity to escape a few days ago and reported to the French Concession Police Station, requesting assistance. Detective Qin Youyu, dispatched by the police chief, investigated and found that the madam Tang Chen not only forced good women into prostitution, but also opened a brothel without obtaining a license from the Shanghai Municipal Council, which violated both criminal law and regulations. She was arrested and reported to the police chief, and taken into custody.

Yesterday, she was sent to the Second Special District Court, where Judge Wu Fanglian conducted the trial. The police lawyer prosecuted Tang Chen for offenses against morality and freedom. After questioning the defendants in court, Tang Chen admitted that she had taken in Ye Jinfeng as a prostitute without obtaining a license. The judge then declared the debate closed, and the defendants were remanded in custody. The sentence is scheduled to be pronounced in three days.

To Recover the Cross-Border Telephone Lines, Both Chinese and Concession Areas Are Increasing Connection Equipment 153

The Number 04 Exchange Connecting Pudong Will Be Completed on the 20th

Thirty Cross-Border Machines in Zhabei and Other Areas Have Been Removed

Since the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation negotiated with the Shanghai Telephone Company to recover the cross-border telephone lines, it could have been realized earlier. However, the telephone company's Number 02 manual exchange connecting the Chinese area was quite busy. If it was split off and still connected by the Number 02 manual exchange, it would be even more difficult to cope with. Therefore, the company added a Number 04 manual exchange on the 20th of last month, specifically for connecting the Concession area to Pudong. It is scheduled to be completed on the 20th of this month. All 78 cross-border telephone machines in Pudong this month can be transferred to the telephone bureau for management.

As for the 210 cross-border machines in other areas such as Longhua, Zhenru, Zhabei, Nanshi, and Huxi, in addition to the 30 machines that have been removed by the telephone bureau, the remaining 180 machines must wait until the telephone bureau increases the number of doors on the Number 0 manual exchange in May before they can be removed. The telephone company will also increase the connection equipment to facilitate Chinese and Concession area users to make calls, so as not to wait for a long time.

Unemployed for a Long Time, Driven by Economic Hardship, Posing as a Kidnapper to Extort Money 156

Hou Wenqin: Despicable Yet Pitiful

The Judge Leniently Sentences Him to Four Months

Fan Aisheng, a native of Jiangyin and manager of Dehe Public Indigo Company on Ningbo Road, was kidnapped by bandits five years ago and was ransomed for 5,000 yuan. On the 23rd of last month, at 7:45 PM, he was kidnapped again by bandits at Guangxi Road and Shantou Road, who demanded a huge ransom. After Chief Detective You A'gen of the Old Zha Capture Station rescued Fan from No. 10 Shun'an Lane, West Avenue, and arrested the kidnappers Liu Ziyu, Chou Yulou, and Cui Yaowen, they were handed over to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Details have been published in this newspaper. However, since Fan was kidnapped, the Old Zha Capture Station immediately dispatched Detective Cui Jinchuan and others to guard Fan's house. On the 24th, at 9:45 AM, Fan's house suddenly received a phone call, which was answered by Detective Cui. The caller claimed to be a member of the French Concession police, inquiring whether there was any news about Fan's kidnapping. Detective Cui replied that there was no news. Then the person suddenly changed his tone, saying, "I am actually the leader of the kidnappers. Is your side sincere in negotiating? How much money can you offer?" The detective replied that they were willing to negotiate, but they could not raise a huge sum of money. If it were 5,000 yuan, they could barely manage. However, the other party did not agree, saying that at least 10,000 yuan was required. The detective agreed to try his best and asked to arrange a meeting place and a signal for the person who would come. The other party initially suggested the China Hotel, then the New Guangda Theater, and finally decided on the intersection of Beijing Road and Zhifu Road, in front of the Sino-French Pharmacy, at 2:00 PM.

The person who would come would be wearing a black velvet hat, a long gray cloth gown, a gray scarf, and holding a newspaper. Detective Cui agreed as arranged and reported to the Capture Station. Chief Detective Zhang Yuanqing disguised himself as Fan's representative and waited at the agreed location. Indeed, the person described in the phone call came forward. Before he could speak to Detective Zhang, he was arrested and taken back to the Capture Station. Upon questioning, his name was Hou Wenqin, a native of Shanghai, 20 years old. According to Hou's confession, he had no involvement in the kidnapping incident. He only saw the news about Fan's kidnapping in the newspaper and took advantage of the opportunity to extort money. Because he did not know the phone number, he inquired with the phone company and then called Fan's house from the Shanghai Bank on Ningbo Road. This incident was solely due to economic pressure after being unemployed. The criminal court president of the First Special Court, Mr. Qian Hongye, and Prosecutor Dun Wei opened the court for interrogation. The Capture Station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, stated the case and filed a lawsuit based on Article 363, Section 3 of the Criminal Law, for attempted fraud, requesting that he be punished according to the law. He also stated that the Capture Station confronted the defendant Hou Wenqin with the three captured kidnappers, and all three kidnappers said they did not know Hou. Therefore, it was confirmed that he had no connection with the kidnapping case and was purely opportunistic. Subsequently, Chief Detective Zhang and Detective Cui presented the circumstances of the case in succession. Hou Wenqin confessed to the fraud without denial and said that he was truly young and ignorant, requesting leniency. President Qian reviewed the confession and announced the judgment in court, considering that he was young and a first-time offender, and leniently sentenced him to four months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was final was calculated as two days offsetting one day of imprisonment.

Record of the Rent Reduction Meeting in Daoli Lane 165

The rent set for the houses in Daoli Lane on Fuxu Road in the French Concession is even higher than the market price for similar houses in prosperous areas. Moreover, due to the economic depression, all industries are lifeless, and it is really difficult for the tenants to bear this huge amount of rent. Therefore, a rent reduction movement was launched. Previously, the landlord was requested several times to reduce the original amount by 40%. The tenants elected Mr. Lu to negotiate with the landlord with full authority. As a result, according to Mr. Lu's report at the Second Special District Citizens' Union meeting yesterday, the landlord was willing to reduce each house by five yuan. The tenants found the difference between the requested amount to be too great and difficult to accept. They still nominated Mr. Lu to make further efforts to strive for the landlord, and at the same time hired lawyer Chen Bingxing to engage in legal remedies to achieve the final goal.

Patrol Police Encounter and Arrest Bandit 166

Zhang Zhenwen Accused of Multiple Robberies

The Public Security Bureau of the Fourth District of Zhabei has recently solved many theft cases in succession. Except for those that are currently under investigation and the arrest of the remaining accomplices, which cannot be announced for the time being, around 8:00 PM the night before last, Inspector Li Qingjie of the Taiyang Temple police station dispatched Police Chief Yang Jintang, leading policemen Zhang Qingquan, Zhang Shengsan, Yuan Huizhang, and Li Yutang, to patrol Taiyang Temple Road and Changxing Road (the newly opened, unfinished road north of the Jiajun Guild Hall). They encountered two suspicious bandits. As the police officers were about to step forward to question them, one of the bandits took out a pistol from his pocket. Before he could fire, he was bravely embraced by a police officer. The other bandit took the opportunity to escape. Because the address was desolate and in the dark, he could not be chased. Therefore, the pistol in the hand of the captured bandit was seized. The number was checked to be 241067, a Browning pistol with three bullets. After taking him to the station, it was said that his name was Zhang Zhenwen, 32 years old, from Anhui. Today, he intended to go to Xiaoshadu to rob, and he was not doing a case there, etc. Inspector Li immediately ordered that he be escorted to the Fourth District. Upon questioning, the bandit confessed that he lived in the stove room at No. 38 Jinxiu Lane, Changxing Road, and cohabited with Liu San, who was on the run. The questioning officer immediately ordered the detective team to search his home, but nothing was found. Only a doorplate was retrieved, with the name Liu Ziqing (i.e., Liu San) written on it. Upon further questioning, the bandit confessed that he had robbed a cigarette paper shop on Baoxing Road in the Fifth District, obtaining more than 50 yuan; more than 20 days ago, he had robbed a small hotel on Qingyun Road, obtaining more than 10 yuan; a glass factory and an old woman on Zhongxing Road, obtaining several yuan and two gold rings; seven or eight days ago, he had robbed a rice shop on Jiaotong Road, obtaining one gold ring and more than 20 cents. All of the above robberies were carried out with Liu San and Zhang Zhaoyu, who had already returned to his hometown. The pistol belonged to Liu San. After reviewing the confession, the questioning officer, considering that the bandit had repeatedly committed robbery cases, should be detained temporarily and sent to the Public Security Bureau for transfer to the Shanghai Local Court for punishment.

Lawsuit for Infringing on Talc Powder Brand Name 167

Tongrenhe Paint Shop on Fahua Minguo Road was founded in the Tongzhi period of the late Qing Dynasty and also sold Guangfeng brand talc powder from Guangdong, with flourishing business. In the spring of last year, it was discovered that Shen Taiyuan on Beijing Road was infringing on the brand name talc powder and selling it on the market. Xu Chengxun, the manager of Tongrenhe, originally intended to investigate deeply, but after Lu Zhonglian came forward to mediate, Shen Taiyuan published an apology in the newspaper and compensated for the loss. Now, after several months, it was again discovered that the talc powder boxes sold by Shen Taiyuan were infringing on Tongrenhe's registered Guangfeng brand trademark imitations, and attached a copy of the license registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in the name of Cao Hongzhang, and the paper was printed with the words "Registered Shanghai Wholesale Location: Zhangshou Lane, Qiujiang Road". Tongrenhe then ordered people to investigate. There was only a small school, no shop assistants and no inventory. The shop then considered that Wang Shaoqing, the manager of Shen Taiyuan, and Cao Hongzhang were suspected of colluding to set up a fictitious firm name, and then hired lawyers Fei Guoxi and Jiang Rong to accuse Wang and Cao of harming the business community in the First Special Court. The court opened the trial the other day, because it still needs to be investigated, the date was changed for another trial. However, Cao Hongzhang suddenly submitted a statement to the Second Special Court, accusing Xu Chengxun of counterfeiting the trademark. The court opened yesterday, and the defendant requested a joint trial. Because the First Special Court was related to this case, the court requested instructions and then ordered the proceedings to await the decision of the First Special Court.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the area around Shandong is cloudy with snow and variable winds. The Yangtze River basin and this area are cloudy with fog and drizzling rain or snow. The wind is from the northwest to the northeast. Letters to the Editor 175

To the esteemed editor: Upon reading today's local news section of your newspaper, which reported the arrest of Weng Yuanfan, an employee of our association in charge of weights and measures, for embezzlement, the report stated that this matter was discovered by the chairman of our association, Lu Wenshao, after checking the accounts with the Weights and Measures Inspection Bureau and obtaining conclusive evidence. This is slightly inconsistent with the facts. Our association's weights and measures have always been managed by employee Weng Yuanfan. During the recent re-election of executive committee members, as the old and new committees transitioned, an inventory of the stored weights and measures was conducted, and it was discovered that the employee had "fraudulently" embezzled proceeds from the sale of the equipment, totaling 130 yuan. In addition, there were also instruments that had not been inspected and were sold to colleagues without proper authorization. This matter is of great significance. Because the employee committed embezzlement and violated criminal law, employee Weng Yuanfan and three account books were sent to the No. 1 District and No. 2 Branch Public Security Bureau for investigation. At the same time, a formal lawsuit was filed with the court. This is the course of events handled by our association, which is slightly inconsistent with the details reported in the newspaper. Therefore, we are sending this letter and respectfully request the chief editor to publish this letter in order to make a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Rice Industry Association, February 1st.

To the esteemed editor: I recently read on the fourth page of your newspaper that an airplane crashed in Hongqiao the day before yesterday, with very detailed descriptions. After investigation, not only has there been no such incident here, but there has also been no news of it. I am very shocked, and today there have been many inquiries from various places after seeing the report. However, there is definitely no such thing here. I hereby request a correction to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Hongqiao Aerodrome, Aviation Administration of the Military Commission, February 1st.

To the editor: I read in the local news section of your newspaper on January 31, 1934, about my dangerous situation of being kidnapped, which is not consistent with the facts. I am afraid that the rumors are false, the truth is unknown, and the audience is confused, which has a significant impact. Therefore, I am hereby providing the points of inconsistency, as follows: Dehe Gongji Dye Shop is not opened by me as a shareholder, but I am only an employee of the company. I respectfully request that the above-mentioned points of inconsistency be corrected and published in the "Letters to the Editor" column. I would be most grateful. Sincerely, Fan Aisheng, Shanghai, February 1, 1934.

To the esteemed editor: In the local section of your newspaper on the 29th of last month, it was published that Dinghua Paper Flower Shop in Mayuan Lane, Xiaodongmen, was negligent and attempted to claim fire insurance. Upon investigation, the items sold in our shop are all made of silk, satin, and paper. Due to a careless ember, a fire broke out. Moreover, our shop's business is still good, and we would never resort to such self-destructive behavior. The Public Security Bureau has also inquired and released us, confirming that it was an accident. I respectfully request that you make a correction. I am deeply grateful. Sincerely, Yao Hanming, Shopkeeper.

Reading and Low-Grade Tastes (I) 176

Reading Guidance (Continued)

Nevertheless, I often feel presumptuous in trying to guide people, urging them not to waste their time on these mind-numbing wastes. However, because I lack the scholarly ability to critique, I can never convince them. A relatively difficult book, for example, The Slaughterhouse! I once borrowed it from the library. I eagerly opened it to read, but I found it very difficult, the sentences were too long, not in line with my previous reading habits, and the place names and personal names were all so unfamiliar that I had to reduce my interest considerably. Although I got a lot of help from "Little Kai", which reduced some of the difficulties, it was too much trouble to read such a novel so laboriously. I could only feel a "bitter smile". Of course, this is not a current difficulty, this difficulty has long been overcome by me.

However, I still lack the ability to overcome the difficulties of others. But from experience, I realized that they are obscured by a low-grade taste. They can still be overcome, they can still regain the light; and they urgently need light.

However, in order to overthrow the low-grade taste, there must first be a high-grade taste to replace it. How can we overcome the current "high-grade" "difficulty" in order to make "high-grade" have "taste"? To make people persuaded, you have to dig up the roots of those "weeds", and don't think that the grasslands that have been burned by fire will not happen again in the spring. On this point, we have to make another effort to popularize criticism of the poisons of the old and new Mandarin Duck Butterfly school!

Sir, the words are too incoherent. In summary, it is just one sentence: How to improve the general taste. Although, this project is only fit for you to do, and should be done now. Only when this point is achieved will your work not be serving a few people. The small clerks and apprentices have only received your gift.

What needs to be liberated is the taste of the vast number of apprentices and clerks. Although I have a half-knowledge and a half-understanding, I just feel that I don't know how to do it. The above opinions are entirely mine, but the text was drafted for me by "Little Kai", because I am afraid that the book does not express my intentions and cannot make you fully understand, not because I am afraid that the writing is not smooth and I will lose face.

Finally, I respectfully request that you do not hesitate to provide detailed guidance and corrections.

Ministry of Education Emphasizes Social Education 178

(Nanjing, 1st) According to the request of the China Social Education Society, the Ministry of Education has issued an order to increase the funding for social education and train talents. On the 1st, it ordered all provinces and cities where the funding for social education has not reached the prescribed standard to step up efforts to increase the funding and strive to meet the standard. Those that have real difficulties and cannot immediately meet the standard should also formulate a plan for increasing funding year by year, and report it for assessment. The training of social education talents is also extremely important. In provinces and cities that have established training institutions, the process of establishment and the latest training status should be reported on time. Those that have not yet established training institutions should earnestly plan to establish them and submit a plan for assessment in advance. The Ministry of Education ordered all departments and bureaus to consult with the provincial governments on the following points of the annual meeting resolutions reported by the China Social Education Society: 1. The county governments should be ordered to instruct all public officials in the location of civil education institutions to do their best to assist in the progress of civil education and to establish assessment methods to assign responsibilities. 2. All provinces should be ordered to organize overseas social education and rural education inspection groups, with one or two people from each province joining several provinces to organize. The inspection funds should be allocated by each province as appropriate. 3. All provinces and cities should be ordered to instruct social education institutions to pay attention to object teaching and film teaching. After investigation, the above three proposals are all aimed at promoting and advancing social education. Except for the part of the third proposal related to the Film Censorship Committee, which has been instructed to comply with the Ministry of Internal Affairs, all the original first and third proposals should be followed and implemented. In addition to the separate orders, the original resolutions will be printed and distributed for compliance.

Children of County Magistrates Who Died in the Suppression of Bandits in Jiangxi Are Exempted from Tuition Fees at National Universities 179

(Nanjing, 1st) The Ministry of Education ordered all national universities to approve the temporary regulations on the compensation of county magistrates who died in the suppression of bandits in Jiangxi Province, which were sent by the Jiangxi Provincial Government. A circular was issued to all national universities to exempt the children of deceased county magistrates from tuition fees. The procedures for applying for exemption from fees should temporarily refer to Article 6 of the Temporary Regulations on Exemption from Fees for the Children of Revolutionary Heroes, and a certificate of compensation or other supporting documents should be submitted when applying for exemption to serve as the basis for verification.
