Overview of Education in Zhejiang Province (1) 182

Summary of Two Speeches by Education Ministry Inspector Dai Xia

Education Ministry Inspector Dai Xia returned from inspecting education in Zhejiang Province and gave a speech on the Central Radio Station's wireless platform last week. This Monday, he gave a report at the Ministry of Education's memorial week. The content of the two speeches differed slightly. We have received his summary of the key points of the two speeches, which are recorded below:

(1) On Education Administration

The organization of education administrative organs at all levels in the province is generally sound, the implementation of laws and regulations is considered earnest, and various regulations and administrative policies and plans are mostly practical and feasible. Among them, the guidance conference and the education bureau chief's rural inspection system are particularly outstanding and worthy of our reference. The purpose of the guidance conference is to promote elementary education and social education. Its organization is divided into four levels: province, provincial school district (roughly divided into eleven school districts based on the old prefectural districts), county/city, and county/city school district. The guidance conference is chaired by the Department of Education as the initiating body. The provincial school district guidance conferences are respectively chaired by the affiliated elementary schools of provincial middle schools and the provincial or substitute social education guidance institutions. The county/city guidance conferences are chaired by the county/city education bureaus, all of which serve as connecting hubs. The basic organization is the county/city school district guidance conference, chaired by the central elementary school and the county-run public education center or county-run central public school to discuss various practical issues related to elementary education and social education. This system has been implemented for four years, and the work is relatively intensive. The efficiency of elementary and social education has increased significantly as a result. The second is the system of rural inspections by education bureau chiefs. It is currently stipulated that the education bureau chiefs of each county and city should spend four weeks of each semester inspecting rural areas. Their task is to conduct spot checks and rectify the work of various education institutions, investigate the financial situation of education in various rural areas, pay attention to the communication between education institutions and the public, and, when necessary, convene talks with township chiefs and other relevant people on urging the establishment of more schools and filling enrollment quotas, or visit enthusiastic education or public-spirited gentry to exchange views on improving education. This system has just been announced and implemented for a short time, but it will definitely achieve satisfactory results in the future.

(2) On Education Funding

The total amount of education funding in the province was more than 2.83 million yuan in the 20th year of the Republic (1931). In the 21st year (1932), due to the implementation of austerity measures, only more than 2.24 million yuan was spent. This year, it has been further reduced to 2,106,436 yuan. The amount of funding is not very abundant, and it is decreasing year by year. The financial difficulties are obvious. However, various education programs in the province have been able to not only maintain their original state but also make reasonable progress in both quality and quantity under this extremely tight economic situation, which is commendable. However, it is also inevitable that various facilities have not been able to be fully developed due to the shortage of funds.

Although the province's finances have been extremely difficult over the years, education funds have been prioritized for allocation. However, the independence of education funding has been repeatedly urged by the Ministry of Education recently, and the provincial authorities also feel the need to stabilize education funding. Therefore, they have formulated measures to realize it in stages. The main points are to designate 1.2 million yuan annually from the tax on foil products, about 200,000 yuan annually from the tobacco and alcohol surtax, and about 600,000 yuan annually from the slaughter tax, totaling about 2 million yuan, as special funds for provincial education, to be implemented in three phases. From May of next year, it can be completely independent. The issue of independent education funding has come to an end.

The sources of local education funding are quite complex. The main ones are: 40% of the education tax, surcharges on land tax in the upper and lower periods, grain tax per mu, slaughter tax, property transfer deed tax, local product tax, commercial subsidy tax, superstition tax, consumption tax, luxury tax, and other miscellaneous taxes. The total amount is 3,007,251 yuan. Among the counties, the expenditure on education is the highest at 284,113 yuan and the lowest at 5,649 yuan. Except for a few counties, the education funding in most counties was originally very tight. Moreover, most of them have experienced reduced income due to the impact of the rural economic decline, and most counties have accumulated excessive debts over the years, making rectification even more difficult. The Department of Education is urgently seeking remedies. In terms of increasing revenue, it has already submitted a request to the government to allocate 20% of the newly added local taxes in the future to supplement local education funding. It is expected that there will be a large amount of additional funding. As for rectification, detailed measures have also been formulated and supervised to be implemented, but so far, no significant results have been achieved, and further efforts are still needed.

(3) On Higher Education

In addition to national and private schools, the province only has one provincial higher education institution, the Medical and Pharmaceutical Vocational School. The school has a long history and its management is practical. Graduates also have good career prospects. However, in recent years, due to financial constraints, medical and scientific equipment has not been fully perfected. (To be continued)

Current Status of Education in Jiangxi Province (4) 183

Report by Education Ministry Commissioner Li Ximou

9. Free Education Measures and Scholarships

The scholarship and free education measures in Jiangxi Province are similar to those in Anhui Province. There are government-funded quotas for studying abroad, scholarships for universities outside the province, and grants for secondary schools and above within the province. Rural normal schools are exempt from all tuition and board fees, and normal schools are exempt from tuition fees and subsidized for half of the board fees. The various measures are described as follows: (A) "On the Implementation of Overseas Study Education and Improvement Policies." Jiangxi Province's overseas students are divided into two types: those studying in Japan and those studying in Europe and the United States. The expenses for students studying in Japan are supplemented according to the regulations for managing overseas students in Japan. Government-funded students who are admitted to various imperial universities in Japan, Tokyo Institute of Technology, Tokyo University of Commerce, Chiba Medical University, Tokyo University of Arts and Sciences, Keio University's Faculty of Science, Waseda University's Faculty of Science and Engineering, and Japan Women's University (all of the above universities are limited to undergraduates) are given 84 yen per month. Those who are admitted to Fukuoka Meiji Vocational School, Ueda Sericulture Vocational School, Chiba Medical University's Pharmaceutical Department, Tokyo Ueno Music School, Tokyo Ueno Art School, Tokyo Higher Normal School, Tokyo Women's Higher Normal School, Nara Women's Higher Normal School, Japan's National First to Eighth Higher Schools, Fukushima Higher Normal School, Tokyo Women's Medical Vocational School (all of the above schools are limited to undergraduates), and Tokyo Institute of Technology Preparatory School, Tokyo University of Commerce Preparatory School are given 76 yen per month. As for subsidies, self-funded students from this province who are admitted to the first year or above of undergraduate studies in higher vocational schools and private universities in Japan, and female students who are studying in the vocational departments of official or private vocational schools and above are eligible for supplementation. The fixed number is 15, with each person receiving 17 yen per month. There are 10 subsidy students. The qualifications are those who have obtained the Japanese Ministry of Education's G-type funding to study in university undergraduate programs, receiving 14 yen per month, or those who are studying in higher or vocational schools or university preparatory courses, receiving 6 yen per month. Government-funded students in Europe and the United States are selected by the Department of Education and are not supplemented. The quota is set at 5 for the United States, 2 for the United Kingdom, 2 for France, 2 for Germany, and 3 for other countries. Each person in the United States receives 90 US dollars per month, the United Kingdom 20 pounds, France 1,800 francs, and Germany 360 marks. Other countries are determined on a temporary basis. The cost of going abroad and outfitting is a total of 1,000 yuan in national currency per person, and the cost of returning home is 600 yuan. The number of subsidy students is set at 8 for the United States, 2 for the United Kingdom, 8 for France, 3 for Germany, and 4 for other countries. The amount paid to each person is based on one-third of the government-funded students in that country. However, since the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese Incident, students studying in Japan have returned to the country one after another, requesting to transfer to other schools. The Department of Education has formulated interim measures for transferring to schools at home and abroad, and it has been decided that those who transfer to Europe and the United States will be treated with half of the government funding (half of the government funding for Europe and the United States). There are a total of 8 people, including Wan Quansheng (4 of whom have not yet gone abroad). Most of the remaining students have returned to Japan to resume their studies. As for government-funded subsidy students studying in Europe and the United States, many have also returned home after their terms have expired. In order to reorganize overseas education and clear up arrears, the Department of Education has submitted a proposal to the Provincial Government Committee, which has decided that from May of the 21st year (1932), regardless of whether they are government-funded or subsidy students in the East or West, and the vacant quotas for subsidies for studying in Japan, all will be temporarily suspended. This has been forwarded for compliance. Currently, there are more than 39,000 yuan in arrears for overseas study expenses, which have been paid off. It is planned to hold an examination for government-funded students to study in Europe and the United States once next year. The subjects will be limited to talents that meet the needs of the province. The overseas study expenses and the current list of overseas students are recorded below. (1) "Overseas Study Budget and Comparison for the 22nd Year (1933)." The overseas study expenses for Japan in the 21st year (1932) were 113,614 yuan, while in the 22nd year (1933) it was 78,621 yuan, a decrease of 34,993 yuan compared to the 21st year (1932). The overseas study expenses for Europe and the United States in the 21st year (1932) were 65,388 yuan, while in the 22nd year (1933) it was 64,106 yuan, a decrease of 1,282 yuan compared to the 21st year (1932). (2) "Statistics of Government-Funded and Subsidy Students Studying Abroad." There are 64 government-funded students in Japan, 1 in the UK, and 2 in Germany. There are 3 half-government-funded students in Germany and 1 in France. There are 5 subsidy students in Japan, 1 in Germany, 7 in France, and 3 in the United States. There is 1 student in Switzerland. There is 1 subsidy student in Japan. (B) "On Scholarship Measures and Improvement Opinions." Jiangxi Province has formulated scholarship measures for self-funded students studying in Europe and the United States, stipulating that the scholarship amount is 10 names. The qualifications are those who are studying in the first year or above of a university graduate school and have special achievements, and the subjects they are studying must meet the needs of the province. Those who apply for scholarships must submit their documents to the Department for review before July 31st of each year and submit them to the Ministry of Education for approval. The amount is 30 US dollars per month for each person in the United States, 120 marks in Germany, 600 francs in France, and 6 pounds in the United Kingdom. Other countries are determined on a temporary basis. The maximum period for receiving the scholarship is no more than three years. The above measures have been announced and implemented in September of this year. Currently, students from Jiangxi who are studying in various countries are requesting scholarships, and most of them are studying in liberal arts and law. In order to encourage talents in practical subjects, the Department of Education plans to prioritize supplementation for those who are studying in engineering, agriculture, science, and medicine in order to meet the needs and pay special attention to students with excellent grades. (C) "Measures for Grants to Students in Secondary Schools and Above." In the past, secondary schools and above once established scholarships, but they were suspended due to financial difficulties. In October of the 21st year (1932), the previous measures were revised and renamed the Grant Regulations. The total amount is still 20,000 yuan. All schools are ordered to report 5% of the total number of students in the school. Those who pass the review by the Department of Education are divided into three grades: A, B, and C, and given grants. These measures have been effectively implemented. (D) "Revised Regulations on Scholarships for Students from Jiangxi Province Studying in Universities and Vocational Schools Outside the Province." Students from Jiangxi Province who are studying in national universities or vocational schools outside the province have previously established regulations for subsidies to provide assistance. However, the regulations do not have a limit on the number of students. All students from Jiangxi Province, except those who are repeating a grade, can receive the subsidies. In recent years, the number of students from Jiangxi Province who have been admitted to universities and vocational schools outside the province has increased sharply, resulting in a huge shortfall in the original budget for subsidies. Moreover, this kind of general subsidy measure is not in line with the government's purpose of rewarding and educating the talents needed today. Therefore, it has been specially revised and changed to scholarship regulations, which are classified by department and limit the number of students, and will be effectively implemented from the 22nd year (1933). The province has revised the Regulations on Scholarships for Students from Jiangxi Province Studying in Universities and Vocational Schools Outside the Province, which have ten articles. The main points are: (1) Set up scholarship quotas for students from Jiangxi Province in various universities and vocational schools: (A) National Universities, University Graduate Schools, Vocational Schools. (B) Private Jinling University's Department of Agriculture, Nankai University's College of Science, Xiehe Medical College, Nantong University's Textile Department. (C) Vocational schools and above that are decided by the Department of Education at the Provincial Affairs Conference according to local needs. (2) The scholarship quota is set at 400 students. Before the existing subsidy students are terminated, they will be supplemented in four phases. The first phase is 50 new students in the 22nd year (1933), the second phase is 90 additional students in the 23rd year (1934), the third phase is 120 additional students in the 24th year (1935), and the fourth phase is 140 additional students in the 25th year (1936). In the future, vacancies will be filled as they occur. (3) The distribution of scholarship quotas: engineering accounts for 20%, agriculture 15%, science 15%, medicine 10%, commerce and law 10%, art 5%, physical education 5%, home economics 5%, and literature, philosophy, and education 5%. (4) Students from Jiangxi Province who are handled in accordance with the regulations and pass the review by the Department of Education can apply for scholarships of 100 yuan per year per person. (5) If the number of students applying for scholarships exceeds the stipulated quota, the Department of Education will follow the following methods: (A) University Graduate School before University. (B) National University before Private University. (C) University before Vocational School. (D) If schools are equal, upper grades before lower grades. (E) If grades are equal, the order is determined by the level of achievement. (The End)

The Executive Yuan Will Convene a Joint Meeting of Gengkuan Agencies 184

The Secretariat Has Informed Them to Immediately Submit Expenditure Budgets for the Next Year

In recent years, the Boxer Indemnity that China was supposed to pay to various countries has been returned one after another by the countries concerned. In principle, most of it is stipulated to be used for education and cultural undertakings. However, the number returned by each country each year is indeed not small. The outside world is mostly unclear about the management methods and use of these funds. The Shanghai Education Association once submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to clearly stipulate unified management methods for the Boxer Indemnity returned by various countries and to publish detailed annual income and expenditure information. The Central Political Conference also decided at its 372nd meeting to hand it over to the Executive Yuan for proper handling. The Executive Yuan then convened a meeting of representatives from various Gengkuan agencies on November 6th of last year, including Li Shizeng, Zhang Renjie, Ren Hongjun, Shi Ying, Zhu Jiahua, Li Shuhua, and Zeng Rongpu, totaling more than ten people. At the same time, representatives from the Ministry of Finance, the Auditing Department, and the Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, as well as Minister of Education Wang Shijie, Vice Minister Duan Xipeng, Secretary-General Chu Minyi, and Director of Political Affairs Peng Xuepei were invited to attend the discussion. In addition to Chairman Wang of the Executive Yuan reporting on the purpose of the meeting, representatives from various Gengkuan agencies also reported on the situation of their respective agencies. The results of the meeting were very good. A total of three cases were resolved regarding the budget preparation process, two cases regarding reimbursement and auditing, and six cases regarding cooperation between various Gengkuan agencies. It was also decided to hold meetings in March and November of this year. During the adjournment, an office for the joint meeting of Gengkuan agencies was established, with one secretary handling the affairs of the meeting under the order of the President of the Executive Yuan. Now that the time for the March meeting is approaching, Chairman Wang has specially instructed the Secretariat to promptly urge various Gengkuan agencies to prepare the matters to be handled in accordance with the resolutions of the previous meeting. It is reported that the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan has separately notified the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, the Sino-French Education Foundation Committee, the Board of Trustees for the Administration of the British Boxer Indemnity Fund, the Sino-He Boxer Indemnity Committee, and the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee to comply with the instructions. The original letter is copied as follows: By order of the President of the Executive Yuan, it is found that the first item, paragraph 1 of the resolutions of the Gengkuan meeting on November 6th of last year states that each Gengkuan agency must, from the 24th year of the Republic (1935), prepare the budget and explanation of use for the next year of each agency before January 15th of each year and send it to the Executive Yuan for review by the Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics and the Ministry of Education (for the 23rd year (1934), the budget and explanation of use should be sent to the Executive Yuan two months before the original budget preparation period of each agency). Also, the second item, paragraph 3 states that the aforementioned joint meeting will be convened by the Executive Yuan once a year in December from the 24th year of the Republic (1935) to discuss the important principles or other important matters regarding the use of the budget of each Gengkuan agency for education and cultural undertakings (in the 23rd year (1934), meetings will be held in March and December). Paragraph 4 states that each Gengkuan agency... must submit to the Executive Yuan in writing the amount and plan regarding the use of the budget of each agency for education and cultural undertakings for the next year before the meeting. The Secretariat should notify each Gengkuan agency to promptly send the above documents to the Executive Yuan so that they can be presented for discussion at the joint meeting in March, etc. In addition to separate letters, this letter is hereby sent for your information.

Local News

Jinan University's Acting President Shen Pengfei Went to Nanjing Yesterday After Taking Office 186

To Seek Instructions From the Ministry of Education on Reorganizing School Affairs

Will Return to Shanghai Tomorrow Morning and Set the Opening Date for February 5th

Mr. Shen Pengfei, the acting president of National Jinan University, took office at the school at 9:00 AM yesterday and took the night train to Nanjing to seek instructions from the Ministry of Education. He is scheduled to return to Shanghai tomorrow morning. The details are recorded as follows:

Mr. Shen's Arrival at the School: Mr. Shen Pengfei went to Jinan University at 9:00 AM yesterday, accompanied by Secretary-General Feng Tianru and three staff members. The school gate was decorated with the flag of the Party and the nation. The entire committee of the Student School Protection Association lined up to welcome him and led him to inspect the offices of the Student Union. Mr. Shen immediately convened a meeting with the committee members and stated that the students' suggestions for reforming Jinan University could be reviewed and adopted in general. He had decided to find ways to reduce student tuition and miscellaneous fees and had good plans for reorganizing school administration. He also scheduled a speech to the entire student body during the memorial week next Monday to report on his school management policies.

Reception Situation: After the talks, Mr. Huang Zupei, the former director of the school's Finance Department, accompanied him to inspect the school's offices, classrooms, dormitories, and library. Secretary-General Feng Tianhe and Director Huang respectively checked and received the items. However, the registration class was sealed and kept by the Municipal Education Bureau, so it was not received until the afternoon when personnel from the Education Bureau and the Public Security Bureau were dispatched to open the seal together.

Going to Nanjing for Instructions: After taking office, Mr. Shen needed to report the situation of the takeover to the Ministry of Education and seek instructions from the Ministry of Education on reducing student tuition and miscellaneous fees. Therefore, he took a train to Nanjing last night and is scheduled to return to Shanghai on the night train tonight. The student registration matters still need to be decided by the school affairs meeting. The opening date is expected to be around February 5th. In addition to Secretary-General Feng Tianru, who has already been appointed, the other important officials of the school have not yet been announced.

The Art Exhibition at the Municipal Public Education Center Opened Yesterday 188

Divided Into More Than Ten Categories Such as Calligraphy, Painting, Sculpture, and Weaving

Collected Hundreds of Works by Famous Artists From Ancient and Modern Times

The Art Exhibition organized by the Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center, which was previously approved by the Municipal Education Bureau, opened at 9:00 AM yesterday. The exhibition will last for 40 days. The venue is the Health Education Exhibition Room in front of the center. The exhibited works are divided into more than ten categories, such as calligraphy, painting, epigraphy, photography, embroidery, weaving, sculpture, ceramics, pottery, and lacquerware. There are more than 100 pieces of calligraphy and painting by famous artists from ancient and modern times, including He Shisun, Ren Bonian, Luo Hanhua, Ni Mogeng, Cheng Yaosheng, Yao Shuping, Huang Shoushan, Wu Changshuo, Lu Lianfu, Wu Daiqiu, Li Fangyuan, Xie Gongzhan, Yu Jianhua, Gao Shangzhi, Ma Gongyu, Xu Tiefeng, and Huang Jiyuan. The photography includes works by Guo Jingshan and Yong Fuping. In terms of sculpture, there are a pair of marble pots, a pair of large stone lions, two stone wind lanterns, a pair of small stone lions, stone tables, and stone benches, all of which are exquisitely carved. There are dozens of potted plants from the Municipal Garden, the Municipal Botanical Garden, etc., which are very valuable. The collection of embroidery, weaving, epigraphy, ceramics, and pottery is also very rich. Yesterday was the first day of the opening, and from 9:00 AM to 4:00 PM, there were no less than several thousand visitors.

First Prize Is the Complete Elementary School Library

The savings office jointly operated by the Shanghai China Land Reclamation Bank and the Municipal Public Education Center held an essay contest for primary and secondary school students at the end of last year in order to promote student savings. The second-class winners will each receive a silver commemorative coin. Those who are not selected will also receive a watercolor palette as a souvenir. In addition to being announced at the entrance of the Public Education Center, the list of winners will also be sent to their original addresses (those who have not left an address will be sent to their schools). Winners must bring the original letter to receive the award on the award day.

National Shanghai College of Commerce Students' School Protection Movement 191

Preparatory Assembly: Since the Ministry of Education announced the news of the suspension of night schools in Shanghai's universities, students have been extremely alarmed. Students of the National Shanghai College of Commerce's Specialized Department recently convened dozens of classmates to discuss countermeasures and immediately established a Preparatory Committee for the School Protection Association of the Department of Specialized Studies of the College. Many measures were discussed, and five representatives were selected to visit President Pei of the college on the morning of the previous day to inquire about the truth. President Pei received them and gave a speech (the text is recorded separately). After the representatives returned to the meeting at 7:00 PM that night and reported, everyone believed that although the Ministry of Education ordered the gradual closure, the authorities immediately suspended them, and they all believed that the situation was serious and advocated convening a general assembly to discuss everything. It was decided to be held on the evening of February 2nd at 6:00 PM in the Specialized Department's school.

President's Speech: It is briefly stated that the night school system is indeed an urgent facility in view of China's current social situation and to satisfy the thirst for knowledge of the general unemployed youth. I have had a development plan for the night school of this college to benefit the youth and achieve significant results. At the beginning of the current semester, I decided to hire expert professors to enrich the curriculum. I am very happy that the students can understand this intention, work hard, and not slack off, which is gratifying. The Ministry of Education once sent someone to investigate, and the report on the night school of this college was quite satisfactory. Unexpectedly, the order to suspend the school was suddenly issued. As a national university, this college should accept government orders. However, although the Ministry of Education ordered the gradual closure, I have considered this matter several times and felt that the facts and the future are indeed very difficult. Therefore, as soon as I paid attention to the suspension, I had already taken steps to handle the transfer procedures for students' schooling. The representatives then asked him to express his personal opinions, saying that because of my position, it is inconvenient for me to express anything.

▲ Yonggan 25... Feixia 9

The Fan Wangdu team, formerly known as the St. John's University basketball team, defeated Xiaguang 63-19 last night in the Shanghai Basketball League. Minutes of the Closing Meeting of the National Games 200

After the closing of the 22nd National Games, the Preparatory Committee initially retained the Games staff to compile reports. Subsequently, when everything was mostly in order, the committee was closed, and all unfinished matters were handed over to the Physical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education. The committee took advantage of the discussion of the shuttlecock kicking competition and convened a meeting at 8:30 PM on the 31st in the Ministry of Education's conference room to discuss the closing matters of the National Games. Those present included Chu Minyi, Zhang Jiong, Lei Zhen, Zhang Zhijiang (represented by Jiang Rongqiao), Wu Yunrui, Peng Baichuan, Hao Gengsheng, and Guo Lianfeng. Chu Minyi chaired the meeting, discussing the fundraising for insufficient funds and the issue of printing the report. The report will be handed over to the Shanghai Great Book Company for printing. In addition, the originally planned subsidies could not be allocated due to financial difficulties.

Second Capital Shuttlecock Kicking Competition to Be Held on March 3rd and 4th 201

The preparatory committee for the second Capital Shuttlecock Kicking Competition held its first preparatory meeting at 8:00 PM on the 31st in the Ministry of Education's conference room. Those present included Chu Minyi, Zhang Jiong, Peng Baichuan, Hao Gengsheng, Wu Yunrui, Guo Lianfeng, Kuang Yunwen, and Huang Shijie. Chu Minyi chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on the process of holding the first competition last year and the points to note for holding this year's competition. Guo Lianfeng then reported on the donations and the purchase of prizes last year. A total of 507.5 yuan was donated, and prizes worth 299.11 yuan were purchased. After deducting expenses, there was a remaining balance of 208.39 yuan. Discussions then began, and the following resolutions were made: (1) The balance from the previous session will be used to purchase prizes for this competition, and no further fundraising will be conducted. The miscellaneous expenses will still be borne by the Physical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education (two-thirds) and the Beijing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau (one-third), following the precedent of last year. (2) The competition period is scheduled for March 3rd (Saturday) from 3:00 PM to 6:00 PM, and March 4th (Sunday) from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM. (3) The grouping method will be as follows: those under 12 years old will be Group A, and those 13 years old and above will be Group B. (4) The types of competitions will still be divided into plate kicking and exchange kicking. In addition, there will be performance items, with those with the most variations being the winners. (5) The registration period is scheduled from February 17th to 28th. (6) Registration locations are the Central University Gymnasium, the Ministry of Education, the Beijing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Public Sports Field, the Mass Education Center, the Orphans' School, and the Central Military Academy. (7) The competition location is the Central University Gymnasium. (8) The competition rules and registration forms will be handled in accordance with the regulations of last year. (9) The next meeting is scheduled for 8:00 PM on February 28th.

Essays

Involuntary Marriage 202

— Qing Qu

Marriage, as it is discussed now, should naturally emphasize freedom. Because a person's life, with one husband and one wife, is a unit. Only with a happy family can there be a sound society, and only with a sound society can there be a strong nation. Therefore, the reason why everyone must seek freedom in marriage is that it is about the independent sovereignty of a lifetime without defects, and it is also about enjoying complete and equal happiness for a hundred years. If it is not like this, but the marriage contract is concluded, or one does not agree, having listened to parents and the relationship between families since childhood, and then blaming the bad consequences of marrying for status, even to the point of both sides cursing each other's parents, this is truly the bad result of involuntary marriage, which no moralist can deny!

Ah! In fact, that is what is said, but I do not know that on the real wedding day, if you look at the status of the bride and groom, whether they have the qualifications for freedom, I am afraid that they do not think about it, but they will suddenly realize that they want to laugh it off! Because of what? Not to mention anything else, just at the time of the wedding, if you want freedom, it is simply like being a prisoner, unable to move freely. The groom must be invited out by the best man, and the bride sits in the car or in the sedan chair, and even more must be supported by the bridesmaid before daring to get up and take a step. No! They can only sit silently in the inside, unable to make a sound, losing their freedom to the extreme. And the fashionable people still talk about "free marriage," and they are infinitely envious, thinking that freedom is at this time. Alas! In fact, it is a real misjudgment! You! Do not see the master of ceremonies standing on a high stool, he is still holding a scarlet etiquette list in his hand, if he does not shout loudly, no one dares to move, so this master of ceremonies, at that time, wields the supreme authority of the whole hall. He shouts to play music, and the drums and music will start to play loudly. He shouts for that one to take a seat, and the guests, introducers, and the presiding and officiating parties also enter one after another. And the bride and groom will even look at the tip of their noses, under the gazes of the audience, slowly being led by the best man and bridesmaid to the same standing ground, not daring to laugh, not raising their heads, listening to people shouting like this, and doing like this. Look at this time, is there any freedom in marriage? If the master of ceremonies does not shout to retreat, no one dares to retreat, even the officiating person must be an elder of mature wisdom and prestige, whose age will of course not be young, and must also follow the master of ceremonies' slogan, otherwise, they will stand there blankly, standing for at least half an hour, and even if their feet are cold and their legs are sore, they still do not dare to leave on their own. Therefore, others say "free marriage," but I insist on saying the opposite, calling it "involuntary marriage." The old-fashioned etiquette of the past was indeed not very good, but now I also feel that there are many meaningless formalities, such as exchanging ornaments and using seals, which are just formalities. And the officiating person, from the surface, seems to guarantee the two newlyweds, so how important is it? Therefore, they usually say a few very good words of instruction, "In the future, they will form a new family and be a good model for society." Humph! Unfortunately, before long, they raise the conditions for divorce, but the officiating person has nothing to do with it, and the law will not summon him to ask how he testified at the time. Haha! Then, are not the others all unnecessary?

Winter Morning 203

— Fu Yizhi

The north wind roared and rushed towards me, plunging into my collar, sleeves, and coat lapels, winding its way into my inner self, making me shiver several times. The tin signs in front of the small shops were blown by the wind and swayed uneasily, sometimes even emitting a sharp, grating sound. There were few pedestrians on the road. Rickshaw pullers could not find customers and dragged their empty vehicles listlessly toward the vast path of life. The men wore torn felt hats, and the women wrapped themselves in floral cloth scarves, carrying loads of chives, celery, radishes, and other vegetables to the small vegetable markets to await the arrival of the maids and young ladies. ... Here, there were no essential people to form the prosperity of the city. At this time, one could not even hear the shouts and songs that punctuated the liveliness, like the frontier and ancient city on the eve of a great battle, with only the soldiers fighting for survival desperately digging trenches to meet their enemies. Ah! This is the morning of winter in a metropolis.

People living in the metropolis, filled with shops, residences, and all things moving and still, have long since ceased to know what is meant by the intoxicating and beautifying nature. The vibrant spring and the artistically meaningful autumn can only be understood and appreciated in the embrace of nature, and its creations of beautiful and poetic artistic scenes. However, the scorching summer and the bone-chilling winter, even in a metropolis, can be felt in the same way as in a remote village thatched cottage, and sometimes even more unbearably, especially on such a winter morning. Unless people have heating pipes indoors and Chevrolets outdoors, they will not feel anything. Who says that a prosperous city is a paradise on earth?

At this time, the wind seemed to have conquered everything and was at its most triumphant. The radiant morning sun can often give the poor a lot of warmth and increase people's body temperature, but the wind is often jealous and refuses to let it "show favor." When the morning sun rises roundly and gradually transmits a little warmth to the world, it roars in gusts, causing the morning sun to present only a faint shadow in the thin clouds. It refuses to leave any remaining power and uses all its brutal instincts on the world. Such a solemn and desolate morning is probably the crystallization of its evil deeds!

Record of a Trip to Wuhan 204

— Dai Yuren

I once heard a Western friend say that instead of traveling to the three islands of Japan, it would be better to tour and admire the scenery of the Yangtze River. The scenery of the Yangtze River is natural, and there are many historical sites. Moreover, the equipment on the riverboats is comfortable, and there is no suffering from the wind and waves of the sea. Recently, I went to Hankou on business and stayed for five days. After finishing my work, I had a day off, so I went with a friend across the river to Wuchang, and then hired a car for fifteen miles to Luojia Mountain to visit Wuhan University. The school buildings are built on the mountain, magnificent and unparalleled. To the east is the East Lake, similar to the West Lake of Hangzhou, but cleaner. On the opposite bank, there is a garden and a bee farm, run by a certain banker. The air here is fresh, the scenery is beautiful, and the place is secluded, making it very suitable for studying. I lingered for a long time and returned to Wuchang, climbed the Yellow Crane Tower, and overlooked Hanyang and Hankou. Everything was clearly visible. Reciting the Yellow Crane Tower poems of the ancients to the line "The trees of Hanyang are clearly visible on the sunny riverbank," I immediately crossed the river to Hanyang to find the Qingchuan Pavilion, but it was already dilapidated and could not be climbed. I wanted to visit more places, but unfortunately, it was already evening, and the Jiang'an steamship had sounded its whistle, so I immediately returned to Hankou to board the ship. We set sail at nine o'clock, and at midnight we arrived at Huangzhou, where Su Dongpo used to visit the Red Cliff. The next day, we arrived at Jiujiang, and from afar we saw the towering Mount Lu, with its snow still unmelting, which shows how cold the climate is in the mountains. It is also easy to imagine how cool and comfortable it would be in the summer heat, truly a resort for escaping the summer heat. I also bought several kinds of porcelain, exquisite and antique, not as foreign as imported goods. It is a pity that in recent years, Chinese people prefer to use foreign goods, which has led to the decline of the porcelain industry in Jiangxi, which is deeply regrettable. In the afternoon, the boat passed Pengze. The city walls were built along several peaks, relying on the market and along the river. From the boat, I saw this small city, surrounded by mountains on three sides and facing the river on one side, which was quite like a paradise. Tao Yuanming once served as an official here, drinking wine and writing poetry. What more could one ask for than a Peach Blossom Spring? After another few hours, we passed Xiaogushan Mountain, standing tall in the center of the river, incomparably beautiful. The next day, we only reached Datong. From here, we could take a small boat to Mount Jiuhua (one of the four famous mountains in China). Every summer, pilgrims flock to it. We continued downstream and passed Zhenjiang, where Jiaoshan Mountain stood in the river, similar to Xiaogushan Mountain but larger. It is also one of the ancient scenic spots along the river, but I regretted not having time to visit. From Hankou to Shanghai is the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. Further up to Sichuan and other places is the upper reaches, where the water flows rapidly and is not as easy to navigate as the lower reaches. Along the way, sails are like forests, and there are many mountains and islands, which are very pleasing to the eye and refreshing to the heart. The historical sites in various places can especially evoke memories of the ancients. The words of my Western friend are indeed true. Moreover, the food on the riverboats is exquisite, and the service is attentive, making travel very convenient. It is a pity that many Chinese people prefer to take foreign ships, because Chinese ships are sometimes requisitioned for military service. This time, I took the Jiang'an to Shanghai and felt that everything, especially the food, was more convenient than on foreign ships. Therefore, I dare to introduce it, also to promote state-owned enterprises.

How Many Pairs of Apples? 205

— Xingjian

Question: Now there is a basket of apples. Boy A comes and takes half, plus half a pair. Boy B comes again and takes half a pair. Boy C comes and takes half, plus half a pair. After Boy C takes his share, the apples in the basket are completely gone. Now, how many pairs of apples were there in the basket before any were taken? Answer: There were seven pairs of apples in the basket. Note: Before the answer is revealed, this problem seems completely unreasonable. Each of the boys, A, B, and C, takes half, plus half a pair. No matter what, there must be some apples left in the basket. Now, miraculously, they are all gone. How amazing! Boy A takes half, which is three and a half pairs, plus half a pair, for a total of four pairs. Three pairs remain in the basket. Boy B comes and takes half, which is one and a half pairs, plus half a pair, for a total of two pairs. One pair remains. Boy C comes and takes half, which is half a pair, plus another half a pair, which makes a complete pair. Thus, the apples in the basket are all gone.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 206

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 23: Unbearable Pain, Suspicious, Listening to Drums and Music, Happy and Unharmonious Parting, Urgent Summons Arrived

Therefore, when he came to the backyard that evening, he deliberately took a wide detour, went along the side of the wing room to the window of the main room, moistened his finger with saliva, poked a hole, and looked inside. He saw the son-in-law sleeping on the bed with his clothes on, and his own daughter sitting on the edge of the bed. However, although she was sitting on the edge of the bed, she was twisting her body, leaning on the head of the bed, looking as if she was talking to the son-in-law. The conversation was naturally very long, and it did not seem to end for a long time. Although Jiang was an old woman, she could not help but blush, and she had to open her mouth directly. When she returned home, she thought to herself that the relationship between the two of them was indeed good, but such sweetness was not proper with the father-in-law present. In any case, she had to call her daughter back tomorrow during the day and give her a good scolding. Having made up her mind, the next morning, taking advantage of the fact that Guizhi had come to the main room for dinner, she rushed to the backyard. After entering the door, she was shocked. It turned out that Zhao Ziqiang was not only still the ideal person she imagined, happily there, but also with a sad face, holding a piece of paper in his hands in the middle of the hall, completely lost in thought. He did not even see his mother-in-law coming in. Jiang said with a smile, "Son-in-law, what are you looking at? You seem to be enjoying it." Zhao Ziqiang raised his head, looking surprised, and immediately stuffed the paper into his pocket. With this, Jiang became even more suspicious and asked again, "What are you looking at, son-in-law?" Ziqiang smiled bitterly and replied in a very low voice, "It's a telegram." Jiang said, "Where did the telegram come from?" Ziqiang hesitated for a while and smiled, answering in an extremely low voice, "It's a telegram from our battalion commander. He's calling me to hurry back to defend." Jiang said, "Didn't you ask for two weeks of leave?" Ziqiang said, "According to the dates, the time is almost up. A few days of delay on the road, plus a few days arriving home early, wouldn't that be enough for two weeks? But I also calculated that the days were not enough. It turned out I had asked for three weeks. I don't understand why the battalion commander sent a telegram to urge me before the deadline." (236)

Small Recipes

Common Foods at the End of the Lunar Year 207

— Zhu Yuan

The wind is howling, the snow is fluttering, another picture of the year coming to a close. Although the Gregorian calendar has been promoted for twenty-three years, the Gregorian New Year is just like Christmas for foreigners, without much change in the folk. The twelfth lunar month is noisy, firecrackers crackle, of course, they are lively decorations in the old calendar. The Chinese people's conservatism is naturally unique, not to mention that this New Year's Eve tradition has been passed down from ancestors to future generations!

At the end of the lunar year, the most important thing, of course, is food. In the colorful tea and food shops, every family prepares New Year's food at the end of the year, to be heartily enjoyed.

Large chunks of meat and whole fish are, of course, essential foods for every family. There are also some more exquisite foods that are also essential for every family in Suzhou. Now I write them down below as a timely recipe.

Fried Fish

At the end of the year, the盆碟 used for dishes is indispensable. Although fried fish is an ordinary dish sold on the市場, it is always more expensive than cooking it yourself. So Suzhou people mostly cook it themselves at the end of the year. The cooking method is also very simple. First wash the grass carp or large bream, cut it into thin slices three or four 分 thick, submerge it in a mixture of scallions, ginger, wine, sugar, and soy sauce, soak it for a day or half a day, then take it out and spread it on a扁 (bamboo product) to dry slightly in the shade. Then heat a large pot of oil and fry the fish slices in the油. When the fish is half-cooked, take it out and re-immerse it in a liquid of wine and soy sauce, and then re-enter the pot to cook until it is cooked through. Some people want the fish to have a fragrant aroma, so after the fish is cooked, they smoke it again on wood chips containing spices, and it is done. Use grass carp for cooking fish, the taste is more rich and delicious than bream.

Shrimp Balls

They are indispensable in hot pot. Method: First take out the shrimp meat, then mash the shrimp meat together with shallots and lard in a small stone mortar until the shrimp meat is like mud, then add egg yolks and mash together. (The number of egg yolks depends on the amount of shrimp meat, about half a catty of shrimp meat, add three egg yolks.) After mixing, add a little salt, then boil a pot of 𣺓 water, make the mashed shrimp meat into round balls like桂圓 and put them in the water. Once the shrimp balls are cooked, they will naturally float to the surface of the water and can be scooped up. There is one thing to pay attention to when making shrimp balls: when putting the raw shrimp balls in 𣺓 water, you need to cook them slowly over a gentle fire, otherwise the shrimp balls will be old and not fresh.

Fish Balls

The method of making fish balls is similar to that of shrimp balls, but some procedures are required when taking out the fish脯 to remove the fine bones. The method of taking out the fish脯 is to first cut open a　fish, and then use a knife to scrape flat on the fish meat, so that the fish meat becomes like mud, attached to the knife, and the fine bones of the fish will naturally gradually be exposed, and must be picked out one by one, and then use that kind of fish sauce, put it in a mortar and mash it, add eggs. The eggs mixed in shrimp balls are egg yolks, but fish balls need egg whites. After the fish balls are made, they become snow-white powder balls. In addition to the above three kinds of dishes at the end of the year, there are also egg dumplings, (egg skins wrapped in meat, made into dumpling shapes,)糟雞, etc., and the tasteless bamboo shoots are indispensable in the dishes at the end of the year. There is a saying in Suzhou, called: "If you have not achieved anything in a year, first dust off the dust, if you have not done anything, first buy bamboo shoots." It can also be seen the importance of bamboo shoots.

Now I want to talk about the snacks at the end of the year. The snacks that ordinary people prepare at the end of the year, in addition to the yellow and white cakes purchased in the market, various kinds of lard cakes, (lard cakes, there are several kinds of rose, mint, white sugar, jujube paste, etc., those in tea and food stores are more expensive than those in cake　stores, but their taste is also sweeter and more oily.)饅頭, Ningbo rice cakes, etc., there are also several kinds made by oneself.

Financial Gold Market in Turbulent Times 208

Foreign Telegrams Favorable, Recovered and Rose Five Yuan

Yesterday, a huge storm occurred in the gold market, fluctuating rapidly. Dealers were uncertain and seemed to be in a fog, buying and selling suddenly, making it difficult to handle. In the morning, it fluctuated around 700 yuan, but foreign telegrams from the United States were mostly favorable to the bulls. According to the largest daily price of 706 yuan and the smallest price of 696 yuan and one 角, the difference was 9 yuan and 9 角. As a result, it recovered and rose 5 yuan. Both near and far term silver markets have reported declines. The closing exchange rate for the British pound fell 4.75 分, the US dollar rose 3.5 分, but the gold market opened slightly higher, calculated at 98 yuan and a half. (The opening　situation was extremely chaotic, with a difference of more than ten yuan. It immediately broke through the 700 yuan mark. Suddenly, news came that New York cash reported a rise of half a 角, and the selling momentum was strong. It eventually retraced through the 700 yuan to 690 yuan marks. In an instant, it was learned that the US dollar was not reporting a rise, but was actually a message that it was planned to be raised to 35 yuan, and it had been raised to 98 yuan.) Afterwards, the shorts urgently covered their positions, and the official listing reached 703 yuan and three 角. By the time foreign exchange was firm and then loose again, the banks' willingness to sell was not weak. Hedgers and bulls successively dumped their positions, and eventually fell to 696 yuan and one 角. Afterwards, it fluctuated around 98 and 9 yuan, closing at 7 yuan and 9 角. 4.4 Million Dollars in Coins Minted in January 212

Factory Ingots Totaled 2,800 Less 213

The Auditing Committee of the Central Mint announced yesterday that the new coins of 4.4 million yuan submitted by the Central Mint for examination in January of this year have been inspected by the chemist Mr. Glader, appointed by the Committee, in accordance with the regulations. The fineness and weight are in accordance with the regulations for the coinage of silver standard coins, and certificates have been issued, numbered from 5083 to 5962. In addition, the Class A factory ingots (999 fineness) minted by the Central Mint in January, numbered from 3657 to 3721, totaling 65 ingots, and the Class B factory ingots (880 fineness), numbered from 328 to 3057, totaling 2,730 ingots, have all been "supervised and stamped" by the chemist Mr. Glader, appointed by the Committee, at the time of their "calibration mark", and the fineness and weight of each factory ingot have been listed and registered. In addition to being allowed to leave the factory separately, this announcement is made for public notice.

Securities Market: The Bond Market at 96% Has Become the Center of Speculation 215

Each Bond Fluctuates and Rises by 0.1-0.8 Yuan 216

Yesterday, the market of the Chinese Merchants Stock Exchange was extremely stable, and the overall trend had entered a consolidation phase. The trading volume was also relatively quiet. Although there were large players entering and exiting the market, it was not as active as before. Generally, it will be held for one or two days. Although the number of accounts is huge, there are many profit-taking transactions. Speculators, seeing that short-selling is not the time and that going long is also uninteresting, turned their attention to making large trades on the 96 bonds. Judging from the daily turnover of the 96 bonds in recent days, which is about 2 million, it can be seen the heat of speculation. Yesterday's market price went up all the way. The military reduction bonds rose by 0.8 yuan this month, and the 96 bonds also rose by 0.6 to 0.75 yuan, with the rise almost equal to that of the military reduction bonds. This phenomenon occurs every time the bond market rises to a considerable height. Everyone knows that the 96 bonds have no solutions and no interest, but with a surge of speculation, waves rise by themselves. This is because its bottom is too small and it is easy to stir up. In the morning initial auction yesterday, there seemed to be signs of fatigue. The compilation and reduction were slightly smaller by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. The military reduction 15th was sold, and the 16th was bought, with fierce competition. The market price turned from low to high, and the market sentiment became firm because of this. After that, it was also unanimously returned up by 0.3 to 0.4 yuan. There were many shift trading and profit-taking transactions in the second auction. The military reduction bonds rose by 0.6 yuan, and gradually became weak and flat after entering. The market opened in the afternoon. Many No. 1 sold military reduction bonds, and all items were therefore lackluster, either rising or falling, with very slight fluctuations. The closing price was slightly weaker in the front row and slightly higher by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan in the back row. Generally, it did not break away from the consolidation. The market price resulted in a total rise of 0.1 to 0.8 yuan. The total turnover was 11,128,500 yuan, including 2,000 yuan in spot goods. The total turnover tax for futures was 3,455,000 yuan, 1,940,000 yuan for military reduction bonds, 710,000 yuan for the 19 Customs bonds, 1,260,000 yuan for the 20 Customs bonds, 1,790,000 yuan for the gold short, and 1,500,000 yuan for the 96 bonds. The rest ranged from tens of thousands to 200,000 to 300,000.

July Futures New Wheat Changed to New Measuring Instrument 226

Smaller Than the Old Instrument...Price Discounted by 82% 227

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning and afternoon, the prices of each month remained depressed and trading was scarce. Only recently it was rumored that a certain factory intended to buy and offered good prices, such as the opening prices in March, which were up to $4.12 in the morning and afternoon, an increase of 0.07 yuan compared to the beginning of the week. There were no other transactions. July new wheat traded quite smoothly in the morning and afternoon. However, the firm has implemented a new measuring instrument. It is reported that 500 dan has been changed to 600 dan, which is equivalent to one carload unit. The price is lowered because the new measuring instrument is smaller than the old measuring instrument, roughly at a discount of 82% (the exchange has not yet announced it). Therefore, the price also declined. The opening price was $3.12, and then immediately fell to a little over $3.08. The closing price was $3.10. This new measuring instrument is still new. Internal and external parties must pay attention. Spot prices were held firm because Fuxin and Xingtun were doing the remaining packages, with Shandong red wheat at $4.18, white wheat at $4.15, Taiwan wheat at $4.08 to $4.10, and Bengbu wheat at $4.05. There are few supplies in the market, and the situation looks stable.

Free Talk

Two Enemies 246

— Han Sui

Love affairs should avoid triangles or more complex shapes because if the three parties are equally matched, it becomes a political situation like the Three Kingdoms, lasting for forty or fifty years. War is an even more remarkable thing, but every time I read the newspapers, "head-on assault" isn't so bad, but once it becomes "attacks from both sides," things go badly, with a certain number killed and wounded. Its harm is no less than a soldier's defection or a spy in front of a general. Love is like warfare, and warfare is like writing. A person who is new to writing will definitely discover two enemies: one in their heart and one at the tip of their pen.

Following one's own impulses, charging straight ahead, completely writing out what one wants to say, and if attacking something, certainly bringing the entire force together at the pen tip, like a single blow of a sharp blade, this should be the front line. At the same time, there must be concerns about gains and losses, conciliatory opinions, and feelings of compassion, hindering this pen tip, and this is also a front line. Since being born as a human, one can encounter battles everywhere. Where there is battle, there must arise two kinds of minds: advancing and retreating. Both advance and retreat are possible, and both harmony and war are viable. Only being neither harmonious nor at war is being caught in a pincer attack, the so-called being unable to command and unwilling to obey, which will surely lead to utter defeat, and this is common sense.

But true warriors must also fall into this kind of situation, like Gandhi, like Jesus—"Have compassion on them!" "God give me the power of peace!" Silently whispering—unable to bear the violence inflicted upon themselves, yet unwilling to inflict violence upon those who use violence. Although stemming from a broad mind, it will ultimately lead to great obstacles. This is an extremely high state, rare.

The remedy is to take oneself as the main subject and bring out true strength. Like a brave boxer, allowing ordinary people to hit him without retaliating because he feels the enemy is too small, tolerating him, like a wealthy man losing a small amount of money, not considering it a big deal. This is not failure; waiting until encountering a strong enemy to strike back; or remaining peaceful to the end, bearing crucifixion without complaint, not only not considering the enemy worth mentioning, but also not considering oneself too important. This requires greater strength, true skill. At that time, not only will a pincer attack be ineffective, but even an entire encirclement will fail; a triangle will transform into a congratulatory circle, with oneself casually becoming the center, and the circle will also be determined by oneself.

Remembering Mr. Du Yaquan 247

— Ke Shi

I saw the books written by Mr. Yaquan a long time ago, but I only got to know him about six or seven years ago. At this time, he was only in his fifties, but he was already very thin and old.

Mr. Yaquan loved to talk and loved to laugh. He didn't drink alcohol, but he loved to smoke. He often smoked "Black Girl Brand" cigarettes, which were rolled with brown paper and filled with dark brown tobacco. It is said that ordinary cigarettes often contain picric acid, but this kind of cigarette does not, and the taste is also good. Each conversation often involved various issues, scientific, social, or about the origin of mahjong. He rarely talked about personal matters, because he never calculated his own interests.

When Mr. Yaquan spoke, although his opinions often differed from others, his views were very clear. Once, he heard a speaker talk about the hard lives of people in some reformed countries, and he replied without hesitation:

"That is normal; it is normal for everyone to live a little frugally. It is an abnormal phenomenon when some people enjoy excessive material comforts while most people are starving!"

As he spoke, he nodded, and the smile at the end of his sentence would make the other person feel that their own judgment was inaccurate.

When Mr. Yaquan spoke, he was very concerned about the future of China. I heard such arguments several times: "The Chinese should urgently seek self-sufficiency. If they continue to be exploited by imperialism, the result will be unthinkable." Therefore, he did not like the comprador class, saying that consumer cooperatives should be established. He believed that as long as one explained with reason, one could definitely make it clear, so he later took over a school.

He often talked about this idea to his students, telling them not to become compradors, but the result of this preaching made him very discouraged. He once told me that although there were many good young people, some still dreamed of going to America. Mr. Yaquan was not against studying abroad, but he was afraid that they would not learn anything in America and would instead more easily become compradors.

The school eventually closed down, not entirely due to the discouragement of the organizer; the main reason was that the finances could no longer be sustained. In some schools, the bamboo shoots used in the students' meals were often green and about to turn into bamboo, and when water chestnuts were used, they often already had black spots. But Mr. Yaquan said that young people's food must have sufficient nutrients, so the food must be good. The kitchen said that it was easy to do, just add more money for food. So the money was added. There were many such things. So his several thousand yuan of savings were soon used up, and he had to close the school. But from this experience, he learned how difficult it was to explain a concept.

Soon, the January 28th Incident broke out. He walked out of the firing line, returned to his hometown, and continued to write books. By the summer vacation of last year, he had completed a dictionary of over 700,000 characters, which was written with the help of others. At the end of the summer vacation, he came to Shanghai, and this was my last meeting with him. At this time, he was even older and weaker. Although he still loved to talk, he did not laugh as much as before. While eating, he also told me many things about the countryside.

After that, he sent several more letters. Once, he told me that he had pneumonia, and after treatment, his life was probably no longer in danger, but he still needed to rest for a few days. However, not long after, I received a report from a friend saying that one night, he suddenly worried about many future problems, became too excited, stayed up all night, and the next day, his temperature increased again, and his illness became serious. He passed away on the 6th (last December).

The news came more than a month ago, but when I recall the past, Mr. Yaquan's voice, smile, and appearance are all as if they are right in front of me.

On Tao Yuanming 248

— Gu Yun

Reading Cao Juren's article on painting in the "Free Talk" section of January 30th, there are some remarks about Tao Yuanming. I feel that Duke Tao has been wronged, so I would like to say a few words to correct Mr. Cao.

The original text says: "Although Tao Yuanming might 'cherish a good time and go alone, or plant a staff and weed the fields,' he ultimately 'ascends the east hill to whistle, and composes poems by the clear stream,' not associating with farmers. This kind of pastoral poet is like a white crane in the clouds, occasionally perching in the fields, but actually 'not knowing the difficulty of farming.'"

Yuanming was really a farmer, not just associating with farmers. After he "could not bend his waist for five pecks of rice," he returned to farming until his death. Because he read books and could write poems, he had "whistling" and "composing poems" in his spare time after labor. He had one more skill than ordinary farmers, so he used it for his own enjoyment, just like some laborers today who can hum a few lines of Erhuang opera. What distinguishes him from ordinary poets is precisely that he was a farmer. The parallel between "Tao Xie," "Tao Liu," and "Tao Wei" has always been superficial in writing. How can the lives of Kangle, Liuzhou, and Suzhou be compared to Tao's? Tao's drinking, like Tao's composing poems, was enjoyed only after physical labor. This kind of "enjoyment" is "rest," a rightful need of laborers. All counterfeit farmer poets of the past and present should not steal Duke Tao to compare themselves. Try reading the records about Tao and a volume of Yuanming's poems. His hard work, his stubbornness, his hunger, his poor joy—all jump before our eyes. We don't need to drop book bags, just a few poems that we usually read for fun, such as "Planting beans under the South Mountain, the grass is lush, and the bean seedlings are sparse. Rising early to manage the wasteland, carrying a hoe home by moonlight. The path is narrow, the grass and trees are long, and the evening dew wets my clothes…" "…Holding the plow, I rejoice in the seasonal tasks, turning my face to encourage the farmers… Although I have not measured the year's harvest, I am pleased with the matter at hand. Plowing and planting have their times of rest, and travelers do not inquire. At sunset, we return together, the pot of wine cheers the nearby neighbors…" "…Opening the spring to manage the usual business, the year's work is somewhat impressive… How can the farming family not be bitter? We cannot refuse this difficulty. The four limbs are truly tired, but hopefully, there will be no other troubles. Washing and resting under the eaves, a jug of wine dispels the exhaustion…" "…I only hope it will always be like this; manual labor is not something to sigh about." From these poems, we can see his self-portrait, making it impossible for us to deny that he was a farmer—just a farmer who could write poetry.

Yuanming was certainly a scholar in his youth. The reason why he eventually became a farmer is precisely the expression of his entire thought and personality. The society in which he lived had not yet produced Marx, and there was no awareness or emotion of class struggle. What he benefited from was entirely Confucian thought, expressing the spirit of true Confucianism. He was not without political understanding and ability. But he felt that if one's own behavior was not clean, "eating official rice," "the mind enslaved by the body," then it was fundamentally wrong. Such a person can never engage in politics; doing so would only add a few more corrupt officials. So he would rather till the fields himself, eating the harvest of his own labor. If the harvest was insufficient, suffering from hunger and cold, he would never change. He persisted until his death!

My friend Pan once had this to say about Tao: "Duke Tao's life has a completely consistent spirit. The personality displayed by his strong will is truly a tough, brave, ordinary, and great hero… He could not stand the pretentious and actually despicable atmosphere of the time, and he was unwilling to associate with it. He also did not want 'the mind to be enslaved by the body, greedy for the comfort of the mouth and body.' But in any case, clothing and food must be sought. Since he did not care about 'nibbling on the dregs,' he resolutely became a farmer until his death. This is Duke Tao's extraordinary knowledge, courage, and determination to see the truth and act accordingly. He established a completely consistent system of life on the simplest basis of 'self-labor to seek coarse clothes and plain food'…" (The full text can be found in last year's Beijing Sino-French University Monthly.)

I completely agree with what Pan said, so I quote it as an aid to discussing Tao.

(Postscript) I have never met Mr. Cao. But I often read his clear and vigorous writing in "Free Talk." I often imagine what he is like and admire him. Mr. Cao's article on painting only occasionally mentioned Yuanming in passing and does not occupy an important position in the full text. I mention this because "Free Talk" is not a profound and purely literary publication but a newspaper provided for the general reading public. Also, because what Mr. Cao said made me think of some political figures in China today who are annoying, I am happy to take advantage of Mr. Cao's passing remarks to talk a little about Yuanming. This may be of some benefit to the general public. It is not to criticize Mr. Cao's article. This goes without saying. It is precisely because it is not easy to speak today that I add this footnote.

Morning in the Countryside 249

— He Deming

The morning in the countryside is clear and serene; dew like pearls hangs on the spider webs on the eaves; hangs on the honeylocust and cherry trees in front of the thatched cottage; hangs on the dandelions and foxtails on the grass mounds… The sun reveals its red face on the top of the eastern mountain, and its myriad rays pierce the thin purplish-brown misty coat. Sunlight shines through strings of dewdrops, shimmering like fireflies dancing by the lotus pond on summer nights.

"Little Blackie! Going to the fields so early?"

Uncle Wang is sunbathing on the grass mound, with a dry tobacco pipe in his mouth, speaking to a middle-aged farmer who is leading an ox and carrying a plow and rake.

"Uncle Wang, you're really early."

The middle-aged farmer smiled at Uncle Wang and hurried up the hillside.

"These days, everyone is diligent and hardworking, but the price of rice is falling so much that it's frightening. The price of grain is less than two yuan per load…"

Uncle Wang took a few hearty puffs of his pipe, spitting out circles of smoke, as if lamenting to himself. A black and white cat suddenly ran onto the grass mound. It ran to Uncle Wang's feet and rubbed against him, looking up at Uncle Wang with its eyes, meowing. Uncle Wang gently stroked its head and neck with his pipe, and it gradually became quiet, scratching itself with its own paws.

"Amao! Come quickly to Grandpa."

Uncle Wang stretched his voice and shouted towards the bottom of the grass mound. The crowd at the bottom of the grass mound was as chaotic as a play, with children fighting grass and playing hide-and-seek; middle-aged women picking bean sprouts and shredding radish; and several elderly women mending torn socks and those tattered clothes with a thousand holes…

"Grandpa! Grandpa!…"

Following Uncle Wang's shout, a child of about eight or nine years old ran up from the bottom of the grass mound like an arrow. The child climbed onto his lap, clinging to his sleeve with his left hand, reaching for his beard with his right hand, and shouting "Grandpa" without stopping.

"Amao! Is Grandpa good? Is Mom good?" "Grandpa is good! Grandpa is good!" "Where is Grandpa good?" "Grandpa tells me stories to listen to, gives me sand beans to eat, and roasts sweet potatoes for me…"

"Grandpa is so good, how about giving Grandpa a kiss?" "No! Grandpa has a beard, it will prick my mouth." "If you don't give Grandpa a kiss, Grandpa won't love you!" "Grandpa's beard is like wolfberries, it will prick my mouth!"

"Good Amao, my good Mao Tou, give Grandpa a kiss, please. Give Grandpa a kiss, good boy! Oh, that's a good boy! One more." "No more, it pricks my mouth!"

Amao slid down from Grandpa's lap, touched his mouth, and ran back down the grass mound like an arrow. Uncle Wang watched his grandson run away, picked up his pipe again, and took a deep puff, circles of smoke drifting into the air, drifting, drifting…

"Someone has a basket. If you borrow rice, they will even lend you the carrying pole and rope to carry it back home." "That's good!" "It's really true." Qin Da Niang's reply made Lian Di happy. Third Auntie avoided them, saying, "Qin Da Niang, you can just tell Lian Di what you need to say." "There's nothing to say. Once you're in the city, Lian Di, listen to Third Auntie." She then leaned close to her daughter's ear and said, "Don't forget to change your clothes." Lian Di only nodded, but didn't expect that she would really need to change any clothes. The sky outside had only just brightened a little. The sky was full of gray clouds, and a cold wind was blowing across the desolate fields and the declining village. Qin Da Niang stood on the earthen platform, looked up at the sky, and guessed that it wouldn't rain. In the distance, someone was already stooping over to look for wild vegetables.

Seeing the smiles of Lian Di and Third Auntie, she bravely let her daughter go, hoping that one day she would benefit from her daughter's success.

"Let's go into the city early." "Okay, go into the city with Third Auntie. Remember, listen to Third Auntie, and the clothes." So Lian Di left with Third Auntie with a smile. They said goodbye to each other and wished each other well. After walking a long way, Third Auntie turned her head and said, "I'll pick you up in the city in a while!" Lian Di also turned her head and said, "Mom, wait for me to bring rice home!" Lian Di's voice was full of laughter, and Qin Da Niang could still see her daughter's happy posture in the distance. She turned and entered the door, and grief immediately struck. Her tears streamed down. It was as if a part of her body had suddenly been lost. She couldn't let her daughter go, mourning and blaming herself. She wanted to chase after her immediately and call her daughter back. She immediately stepped out of the threshold, only to see her daughter's figure gradually shrinking. She finally didn't have the courage to utter a single word. She cried sadly, but her daughter had left, and her daughter's figure remained in her heart. That smile before leaving. After a long time, no one comforted her, and she stopped crying, sobbing, with two swollen red eyes, carrying a small broken bamboo basket and a rusty iron shovel, and habitually walked out of the door, preparing to pick wild vegetables.

On the ridges, she looked up at the sky and muttered to herself:

"Why isn't there any sun yet?" (The End)
